Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
3 min
Introduction to al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm
Title page of a foundational introduction to Islamic jurisprudence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and full title of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm, and state its significance as a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh and iftaa.

Core Idea
Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi is a modern classic introducing Islamic jurisprudence with a Hanafi emphasis.

This lesson introduces the opening page of a key modern Hanafi text: al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm by Shaykh Mustafa al-Zarqa. The title page reveals the work's scope, author's credentials, and its role as an entry point for serious study of fiqh and iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Read the full Arabic title
Note the work's principal title: 'al-Fiqh al-Islami fi Thawbihi al-Jadid' and its subtitle 'al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm'. This indicates it is both a fresh presentation of fiqh and a comprehensive introduction.
The term 'Thawbihi al-Jadid' (new garment) signals a modernized arrangement.
2
Identify the author and his credentials
The author is Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, a Syrian Hanafi scholar who taught Islamic Sharia and civil law at Damascus University. His background in both Sharia and civil law gives the work a unique comparative perspective.
3
Recognize the work's structure and purpose
This is Part One of a new edition with revised arrangement and additions. The place of publication is Damascus. The work serves as a foundational text for students of fiqh and iftaa, covering sources, history, and general principles of Islamic jurisprudence.
Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi is often the first text studied in Hanafi iftaa curricula.

Islamic Jurisprudence in its New Garment (1) The General Jurisprudential Introduction New Edition with Development in Arrangement and Classification, and Additions By Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa Former Professor of Islamic Sharia and Civil Law at the College of Sharia and the College of Law at Damascus University Part One Waar al-Qaa Damascus
Source pages p. 1

Commentary
This is the opening page of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm (The General Jurisprudential Introduction) by Shaykh Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa (d. 1999), a prominent Syrian Hanafi scholar and jurist. The page presents the full title of the work: 'Islamic Jurisprudence in its New Garment,' with the subtitle 'The General Jurisprudential Introduction.' It indicates that this is a new edition with revisions in arrangement and additions. The author is identified as a former professor of Islamic Sharia and civil law. This volume is Part One. The place of publication is Damascus. This front matter establishes the identity and scope of the work.

Key Terms
المدخل الفقهي (al-madkhal al-fiqhi): The foundational introduction to Islamic jurisprudence, covering its sources, history, and general principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is the author of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa
C) Ibn 'Abidin
D) Al-Marghinani

Key Takeaway
Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm by Mustafa al-Zarqa is a modern introductory text essential for understanding the foundations of Hanafi fiqh and iftaa.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Need for Systematic Presentation of Islamic Jurisprudence
Foreword praising new systematic presentation of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key challenges in traditional fiqh education and explain how a systematic approach (kulliyat and branches) addresses these challenges, as demonstrated by al-Zarqa's methodology.

Core Idea
Islamic jurisprudence becomes accessible when presented through its general principles and systematic organization.

This foreword by Abdul Qadir Ouda praises the book series 'Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garment' for resolving the difficulties of studying fiqh from traditional texts. The author highlights how the series introduces a modern method of organizing fiqh: presenting general theories and principles (kulliyat) and then deriving branches from them. This approach enables students to grasp the structure of fiqh and apply it to new cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Read the passage to understand why traditional fiqh texts were difficult for students. Look for phrases like 'language closed' and 'style sterile'.
The problem is the inaccessibility of matn and sharh.
2
Identify the solution
Find the description of the new method: 'presenting universals (kulliyat), explaining theories, defining terminology, then deriving branches.'
The solution is systematic organization.
3
Identify the core features
List the three core features mentioned: (1) rooting issues, (2) presenting universals and theories, (3) connecting branches to roots.
This is the essence of the new garment.

تقديم
بقلم : الأستاذ عبد القادر عودة (1)
الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد
كان هذا العنوان أمنيةً فأصبح حقيقة كان أمنية تهوي إليها النفوس وتهفو إليها القلوب، فأصبح حقيقة ماثلة بين دفتي كتاب يستطيع كل قارىء أن ينالها وأن يستمتع بجمالها.
وقبل هذا الكتاب كان عشاق الفقه الإسلامي يحاولون أن ينالوه فلا يستطيع أن يناله منهم إلا البعض وقليل ما هم لأنَّ الفقه اعتصم من طالبيه في المتون، وتحصّن في الشروح واستعصى على طلابه في اللغة المغلقة والأسلوب العقيم.
وكان كل من له إلمام بالفقه الإسلامي، وكل من عانى من قراءة كتب الفقه الإسلامي، يود أن توطأ للناس كتب الفقه حتى يتيسر لهم قراءتها وتسهل عليهم دراستها وحتى يستطيعوا أن يوازنوا بين الفقه الحديث وبين الفقه الإسلامي العتيد، ذلك الفقه الغني بموضوعاته ونظرياته واصطلاحاته المتميز بدقته وقوته ليكون لهم من هذه الموازنة ما يزيد ثقافتهم، ويوسع آفاقهم، ويفتح أعينهم، ويوجههم إلى الطريق المستقيم.
(1) نشر الأستاذ عبد القادر عودة رحمه الله تعالى هذا التقريظ عن الكتاب في مجلة (المسلمون) القاهرة، السنة الثانية، العدد الخامس (١٣٧٢ هـ / ١٩٥٣م ، ص ٤٩٧ - ٥٠٠) . وننشره اليوم تقديماً للكتاب في إخراجه الجديد .

تقديم : للأستاذ عبد القادر عودة
هذه المشاكل التي كانت تواجه عشاق الفقه الإسلامي والدعاة إليه قد حلها كتاب وتلك الأماني التي كانت تجيش بها صدورهم قد حققها كتاب والكتاب الذي حل المشاكل فأحسن حلها وحقق الأماني فأحسن تحقيقها هو كتاب الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد، الذي اتخذنا اسمه عنواناً لهذا المقال.
وإذا صح أن الكتاب يقرأ من عنوانه فهذا الكتاب في نظري أول كتاب يدل عليه عنوانه حق الدلالة ويعبر عنه كل التعبير. إن عنوانه هو الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد وكل عبارة من عباراته، وكل فقرة من فقراته، وكل صفحة من صفحاته هي الفقه الإسلامي في أسلوب جديد وعرض جديد وتنظيم جديد وتوجيه جديد، أو هي الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد كما شاءت الدقة والإحاطة لمؤلفه أن يسميه.
والكتاب سلسلة كتب ظهر منها حتى الآن المدخل الفقهي العام وكتاب الحق والالتزام والأموال والأشخاص، وكتاب عقد البيع، ولا يزال المؤلف يعد كتاب نظرية الالتزام في الفقه الإسلامي. وطريقة المؤلف في الإخراج تدل على أنه سيضيف إلى السلسلة عدداً آخر من الكتب.
ولقد وقع في يدي كتاب المدخل الفقهي العام فوجدت شيئاً جديداً وعملاً جليلاً. فأما أنه شيء جديد فإنه الفقه الإسلامي لم يجر رجاله على هذه الطريقة الحديثة التي جرى عليها المؤلف، ولم يأخذوا بذلك التقسيم العصري الذي أخذ به حيث تؤصل المسائل، وتعرض الكليات وتبسط النظريات وتشرح المصطلحات ثم تستخرج الفروع من أصولها أو ترد الجزئيات إلى كلياتها، أو تطبق النظريات على موضوعاتها فيخرج الدارس من دراسته وقد ألم بالكليات والنظريات وتماسكت في ذهنه المسائل وارتبطت الفروع بالأصول، واستفاد القدرة على حل المشاكل والتمييز بين المتشابه.
،
وأما أنه عمل جليل فلأنه عمل غير مسبوق، ولأنه يقتضي من صاحبه فهماً وعقلاً وجهداً وصبراً حتى يصل إلى ما وصل إليه المؤلف من مستوى
Foreword by Mr. Abdul Qadir Ouda (1). Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garment. This title was a wish that became a reality. It was a wish that souls yearned for and hearts aspired to, and it became a reality manifest between the covers of a book that every reader can attain and enjoy its beauty. Before this book, lovers of Islamic jurisprudence tried to attain it but only a few, and very few, could, because jurisprudence secluded itself from its seekers in the texts (matn), fortified itself in the commentaries, and became inaccessible to its students due to the closed language and sterile style. Everyone who had familiarity with Islamic jurisprudence, and everyone who suffered from reading books of Islamic jurisprudence, wished that the books of jurisprudence would be made easy for people so that they could read them easily, study them readily, and so that they could compare between modern jurisprudence and the ancient Islamic jurisprudence—that jurisprudence rich in its topics, theories, and terminology, distinguished by its precision and strength—so that from this comparison they might increase their culture, broaden their horizons, open their eyes, and guide them to the straight path. (1) Mr. Abdul Qadir Ouda, may Allah have mercy on him, published this commendation of the book in the journal (Al-Muslimun), Cairo, second year, issue five (1372 AH / 1953 AD, pp. 497-500). We republish it today as a foreword to the book in its new edition. : Foreword by Mr. Abdul Qadir Ouda. These problems that faced lovers of Islamic jurisprudence and its callers have been solved by a book, and those wishes that surged in their hearts have been fulfilled by a book. And the book that solved the problems excellently and fulfilled the wishes superbly is the book 'Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garment', whose name we have taken as the title of this article. If it is true that a book is read from its title, then this book, in my view, is the first book that truly indicates its title and expresses it fully. Its title is 'Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garment', and every phrase of its phrases, every paragraph of its paragraphs, every page of its pages is Islamic jurisprudence in a new style, new presentation, new organization, and new direction—or it is Islamic jurisprudence in its new garment, as the precision and comprehensiveness of its author willed him to name it. The book is a series of books, of which so far have appeared: 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm' (General Jurisprudential Introduction), the book of 'Al-Haqq wa al-Iltizam' (Right and Obligation), 'Al-Amwal wa al-Ashkhas' (Wealth and Persons), and the book of 'Aqd al-Bay' (Contract of Sale). The author is still preparing the book 'Nazariyyat al-Iltizam fi al-Fiqh al-Islami' (Theory of Obligation in Islamic Jurisprudence). The author's method of presentation indicates that he will add a number of other books to the series. I came across the book 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm' and found something new and a magnificent work. As for it being something new, it is that Islamic jurisprudence has not been presented by its scholars in this modern method that the author has followed, nor have they adopted the contemporary division that he has adopted, where issues are rooted, universals are presented, theories are expounded, and terminology is explained; then branches are derived from their roots, or particulars are referred back to their universals, or theories are applied to their subjects, so that the student emerges from his study having grasped the universals and theories, the issues cohere in his mind, the branches are connected to their roots, and he gains the ability to solve problems and distinguish between similar cases. And as for it being a magnificent work, it is because it is unprecedented, and because it requires from its author understanding, intellect, effort, and patience until he reaches the level that the author has reached.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is a foreword (تقديم) written by Abdul Qadir Ouda for the book series 'Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garment', specifically for the volume 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm' by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The author praises the series for presenting Islamic jurisprudence in a modern, accessible manner. He contrasts the difficulty of traditional fiqh texts, which relied on dense matn and commentaries, with this new approach that organizes issues systematically, explains general principles (kulliyat) and theories, and connects branches to their roots. The foreword highlights the significance of al-Zarqa's methodology in making fiqh understandable and applicable for contemporary readers. It also lists other volumes in the series: 'Al-Haqq wa al-Iltizam', 'Al-Amwal wa al-Ashkhas', and 'Aqd al-Bay'. The author notes that al-Zarqa is preparing a book on 'Nazariyyat al-Iltizam'. This foreword originally appeared in the journal Al-Muslimun in 1953.

Key Terms
المتون (al-mutun): The core texts of fiqh that are dense and concise, often memorized by students.
الشروح (al-shuruh): Commentaries that explain and expand upon the matn.
الكليات (al-kulliyat): General principles or universals that govern many specific rulings.
الفروع (al-furu'): Specific derived rulings that are applications of the principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the foreword, what is the main achievement of the book 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm'?
A) It simplifies Islamic jurisprudence by presenting it in a modern style with systematic organization of principles and branches.
B) It is a collection of traditional fatwas from Hanafi scholars.
C) It focuses exclusively on the Hanafi school without comparing to other schools.
D) It translates classical texts into English for Western readers.

Key Takeaway
The systematic presentation of Islamic jurisprudence through its general principles (kulliyat) and theories makes it accessible and applicable, a method championed by al-Zarqa.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Importance of Systematic Methodology in Usul al-Iftaa
Praise of a systematic methodology for presenting Islamic jurisprudence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key methodological features of Mustafa al-Zarqa's approach and explain how they facilitate the process of iftaa.

Core Idea
A mufti must ground fatwas in systematic principles — linking branches to roots and organizing rulings into general theories.

This foreword by Abd al-Qadir Awda highlights the revolutionary methodology of Mustafa al-Zarqa in presenting Islamic jurisprudence. For a mufti, understanding this systematic approach is crucial: it ensures that fatwas are not isolated opinions but are derived from coherent principles, enabling consistency and adaptability to new cases. This lesson draws from the foreword to underscore why methodology matters in usul al-iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problems addressed by the author
Read the opening lines to understand the challenges faced by students and callers to Islamic jurisprudence — lack of systematic presentation and difficulty in grasping the subject.
The foreword states that the book solves problems and fulfills hopes.
2
Analyze the methodological features praised
List the key features: presentation in a new style, rooting issues, presenting universals (kulliyat), explaining theories (nazariyat), defining terminology, deriving branches from principles, applying theories to subjects.
These features are directly relevant to usul al-iftaa as they provide a framework for issuing sound fatwas.
3
Relate the methodology to the mufti's work
Consider how these features help a mufti: they enable him to understand the underlying principles, link new cases to established rules, and maintain coherence in his fatwas.
Without such methodology, fatwas risk being arbitrary or contradictory.
4
Appreciate the effort and its significance for iftaa
Reflect on the author's pioneering effort and the scale of the work — it required understanding, intellect, effort, and patience. This mirrors the rigor needed in iftaa.
The foreword emphasizes that such work is unprecedented and requires a collective effort, foreshadowing the collaborative nature of fatwa issuance.

هذه المشاكل التي كانت تواجه عشاق الفقه الإسلامي والدعاة إليه قد حلها كتاب وتلك الأماني التي كانت تجيش بها صدورهم قد حققها كتاب والكتاب الذي حل المشاكل فأحسن حلها وحقق الأماني فأحسن تحقيقها هو كتاب الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد، الذي اتخذنا اسمه عنواناً لهذا المقال.
وإذا صح أن الكتاب يقرأ من عنوانه فهذا الكتاب في نظري أول كتاب يدل عليه عنوانه حق الدلالة ويعبر عنه كل التعبير. إن عنوانه هو الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد وكل عبارة من عباراته، وكل فقرة من فقراته، وكل صفحة من صفحاته هي الفقه الإسلامي في أسلوب جديد وعرض جديد وتنظيم جديد وتوجيه جديد، أو هي الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد كما شاءت الدقة والإحاطة لمؤلفه أن يسميه.
والكتاب سلسلة كتب ظهر منها حتى الآن المدخل الفقهي العام وكتاب الحق والالتزام والأموال والأشخاص، وكتاب عقد البيع، ولا يزال المؤلف يعد كتاب نظرية الالتزام في الفقه الإسلامي. وطريقة المؤلف في الإخراج تدل على أنه سيضيف إلى السلسلة عدداً آخر من الكتب .
ولقد وقع في يدي كتاب المدخل الفقهي العام فوجدت شيئاً جديداً وعملاً جليلاً. فأما أنه شيء جديد فإنه الفقه الإسلامي لم يجر رجاله على هذه الطريقة الحديثة التي جرى عليها المؤلف، ولم يأخذوا بذلك التقسيم العصري الذي أخذ به حيث تؤصل المسائل، وتعرض الكليات وتبسط النظريات وتشرح المصطلحات ثم تستخرج الفروع من أصولها أو ترد الجزئيات إلى كلياتها، أو تطبق النظريات على موضوعاتها فيخرج الدارس من دراسته وقد ألم بالكليات والنظريات وتماسكت في ذهنه المسائل وارتبطت الفروع بالأصول، واستفاد القدرة على حل المشاكل والتمييز بين المتشابه .

رفيع لا يصل إليه عادة إلا النابهون بعد أن تمهد لهم الطرق ويسبقهم الرواد، فإذا ما وصل المؤلف إلى ما وصل إليه بعد أن شق طريقه في الصخر وكان الرائد لنفسه ولغيره، فتلك هي العبقرية الفذة، أو هو فضل الله يؤتيه من يشاء والله ذو الفضل العظيم.
ولقد ساعد المؤلف على الوصول إلى ما وصل إليه، أنه رجل ذو هدف في الحياة وأنه من أصحاب المثل العليا الذين يعملون ويقولون لوجه الله فأمده الله جل شأنه بعونه ورزقه الفهم لدينه وشريعته .
ويلوح أن المؤلف قد عانى من مرارة الاطلاع على كتب الفقه ما عاني، فأخذ على نفسه أن يوطىء الفقه لطلابه ثم رأى الفقه الإسلامي في ترتيبه وتبويبه وربط فروعه بأصوله متأخراً قروناً عن الفقه الحديث، فأخذ على نفسه أن ينقل الفقه الإسلامي عبر هذه القرون الطويلة نقلة واحدة ليلحقه بالفقه الحديث، فوفقه الله إلى ما أراد، فوطأ الفقه الإسلامي لكل طالب، ونقله بخطوة واحدة جبارة من العصر العباسي إلى عصرنا الحديث؛ فإذا هذا الفقه الغني القوي الذي كان ملتفاً في ثوبه العتيق القديم يخرج على الناس في ثوبه الجديد فتيّاً مشرقاً يزاحم الفقه كله بمنكبيه، ويعلن للناس أن فقه الإسلام هو الفقه وأن شريعته هي الشريعة وأن ما اختاره الله للناس هو الخير كل الخير للناس لو كانوا يعلمون .
أن
والمؤلف الجليل يعلم وهو يقدم على هذا العمل الجليل أنه يقدم على عمل أجل وأعظم من أن يقوم به فرد وأن هذا العمل يقتضي تتعاون عليه جهود جماعة من الأساتذة العلماء المطلعين على الفقه الإسلامي والحقوق الحديثة في مصادرها وأساليبها الأجنبية. ولكن الحاجة الملحة إلى السرعة ومسابقة الزمن قضت بأن يقدم على حمل هذا العبء الثقيل الذي ينوء بالعصبة أولي القوة مستمداً من الله العون.
ولقد أمده الله بعونه فوفقه إلى أن يخرج كتاباً جامعاً لأصول الفقه الإسلامي والنظريات العامة التي تبنى عليها الأحكام في لغة قوية تسيل

Foreword by Professor Abd al-Qadir Awda. The problems faced by lovers of Islamic jurisprudence and its callers have been solved by a book, and the hopes they harbored have been realized by a book. The book that solved the problems excellently and realized the hopes excellently is the book 'Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garment', which we have taken as the title of this article. If it is true that a book is known by its title, then this book is, in my view, the first book whose title truly indicates it and fully expresses it. Its title is 'Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garment', and every phrase of its phrases, every paragraph of its paragraphs, and every page of its pages is Islamic jurisprudence in a new style, a new presentation, a new organization, and a new direction; or it is Islamic jurisprudence in its new garment, as the author's precision and comprehensiveness desired him to name it. The book is a series of books that have so far appeared: the General Jurisprudential Introduction, the book on Right and Obligation, Wealth and Persons, and the book on the Contract of Sale. The author is still preparing the book 'Theory of Obligation in Islamic Jurisprudence'. The author's method of production indicates that he will add several more books to the series. I received the book 'General Jurisprudential Introduction' and found something new and a great work. As for it being something new, it is because Islamic jurisprudence has not been conducted by its scholars in this modern method that the author has followed, nor have they adopted the contemporary classification he has adopted, where issues are rooted, universals are presented, theories are simplified, terminology is explained, then branches are derived from their principles, or particulars are referred back to their universals, or theories are applied to their subjects, so that the student emerges from his study having grasped the universals and theories, the issues cohere in his mind, branches are linked to principles, and he gains the ability to solve problems and distinguish between similar matters. As for it being a great work, it is because it is unprecedented, and because it requires from its possessor understanding, intellect, effort, and patience until he reaches the level the author has reached. Foreword by Professor Abd al-Qadir Awda: A high level that is usually reached only by the brilliant after the paths have been paved for them and pioneers have preceded them. So if the author reached what he reached after breaking his path through rock and being a pioneer for himself and others, then that is unique genius, or it is the bounty of Allah that He gives to whom He wills, and Allah is the possessor of great bounty. The author was helped to reach what he reached by being a man with a goal in life and being among people of high ideals who work and speak for the sake of Allah, so Allah Almighty supported him with His help and granted him understanding of His religion and law. It appears that the author suffered the bitterness of studying books of jurisprudence as much as one could, so he took it upon himself to facilitate jurisprudence for its students. Then he saw that Islamic jurisprudence in its arrangement, classification, and linking of branches to principles was centuries behind modern jurisprudence, so he took it upon himself to transport Islamic jurisprudence across these long centuries in one leap to catch up with modern jurisprudence. Allah guided him to what he intended, so he facilitated Islamic jurisprudence for every student and transferred it with one mighty step from the Abbasid era to our modern era. So this rich, strong jurisprudence that was wrapped in its old, ancient garment comes out to people in its new garment, youthful and radiant, competing with all jurisprudence with its shoulders, and declaring to people that the jurisprudence of Islam is the jurisprudence, and its law is the law, and what Allah has chosen for people is the best, all the best for people, if only they knew. That the great author knows, as he undertakes this great work, that he undertakes a work greater and mightier than an individual can accomplish, and that this work requires the cooperation of a group of learned professors knowledgeable about Islamic jurisprudence and modern laws in their foreign sources and methods. But the urgent need for speed and racing against time dictated that he undertake this heavy burden that would overwhelm a band of strong men, seeking help from Allah. And Allah supported him and guided him to produce a comprehensive book on the principles of Islamic jurisprudence and the general theories upon which rulings are built, in a strong flowing language.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is a foreword written by Abd al-Qadir Awda, praising the book 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam' by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The author's methodology is praised for presenting Islamic jurisprudence in a modern, systematic manner, organizing it into general theories and principles, and linking branches to their roots. The commentator highlights that this work is unprecedented and required great effort. The passage also mentions the series of books planned by the author. For a Hanafi usul al-iftaa course, this foreword serves as an introduction to the work's significance and approach. Note: The text includes a repeated section heading and ends abruptly with 'V', likely indicating a page break or incomplete scan.

Key Terms
الكليات (al-kulliyat): Universal principles that govern multiple branches of fiqh, such as 'actions are judged by intentions'.
النظريات (al-nazariyat): General theories that explain the underlying rationale for a set of rulings, e.g., the theory of contract.
تأصيل المسائل (ta'sīl al-masā'il): Rooting issues by tracing them back to their foundational principles (usul).

Key Takeaway
A mufti must adopt a systematic methodology — rooting issues, presenting universals, explaining theories, and deriving branches — to issue consistent and well-grounded fatwas.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Significance of Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm
Praise for the book's methodology and contribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key methodological features of Mustafa al-Zarqa's Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm as described by Abd al-Qadir Awdah, and explain how it bridges classical Hanafi fiqh with modern legal education.

Core Idea
Al-Zarqa makes Islamic jurisprudence accessible to modern law students by presenting it as a system of logical theories.

This preface by Abd al-Qadir Awdah sets the stage for one of the most influential modern introductions to Islamic fiqh. Awdah highlights how al-Zarqa's work fills a critical gap: it presents Hanafi fiqh in a systematic, theory-driven manner that resonates with contemporary legal minds, without sacrificing depth or authenticity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the gap
Recognize that the Islamic library lacked a systematic introduction to fiqh for modern students, as stated: 'this book was the first of its kind missing from the Islamic library.'
2
Identify the method
Note how al-Zarqa links branches (furu) to foundations (usul) and extracts general theories from specific rulings, as described: 'connecting each principle to its branches, extracting from the branches their principles.'
This mirrors the classical usul al-fiqh approach but in a modern theoretical framework.
3
Identify the audience
Appreciate that law students find the book accessible and enjoyable: 'they read it without feeling they are reading something strange or far from them.'
4
Identify the comparative element
Observe the balance between Hanafi fiqh, other madhhabs, and Syrian positive law: 'balances between Islamic schools and between Sharia and Syrian laws.'
This comparative dimension is crucial for iftaa in modern legal systems.
5
Recognize the impact
Understand the book's potential for an Islamic jurisprudential renaissance: 'the first book upon which the Islamic jurisprudential renaissance will be built.'

تقديم : للأستاذ عبد القادر عودة
عذوبة ورقة وفي تنسيق دقيق وترتيب بديع وربط للفروع بالأصول، وسلسلة منطقية للنظريات والأحكام. ولقد كان هذا الكتاب أول الكتب التي تنقص المكتبة الإسلامية، وهو بعد وجوده أول الكتب التي ستبنى عليه النهضة الفقهية الإسلامية فدارس الفقه الإسلامي في حاجة شديدة إلى هذا الكتاب ليعرف الأسس التي يقوم عليها الفقه ولترتبط في ذهنه بعض هذه الأسس بالبعض الآخر ويتوجه بعد ذلك في دراسته توجهاً سليماً.
وأهم ما في الكتاب أن طلبة كلية الحقوق في العالم الإسلامي يستطيعون أن يقرؤوه فلا يشعرون أنهم يقرأون شيئاً غريباً عليهم ولا بعيداً عنهم، بل لعلهم سيجدون في قراءته من اللذة العلمية والتعمق الفقهي ودقة التعبير اللغوي والاصطلاحي ما يجعلهم يفضلونه على غيره من كتب القانون التي تترجم لهم ولا تؤلف، بل لعلهم يجدون فيه من الفن والروح ما لم يجدوه في كتاب آخر.
وقد استطاع المؤلف في سهولة ويسر بما وهبه الله من قوة الفهم وعمق الفقه أن يعرض النظريات الإسلامية العامة كما تعرض النظريات القانونية، وأن يصل كل كلية بفروعها وأن يستخرج من الفروع كلياتها في عمله على المذهب الحنفي، وإن كان يوازن في بعض المسائل بين المذاهب الإسلامية ولا ينسى في أكثر الأحوال أن يوازن بين حكم الشريعة والقوانين السورية .
معتمداً
والكتاب بعد ذلك مرتب ترتيباً منطقياً فالقسم الأول منه يتكلم عن الفقه ومصادره والترتيب التاريخي لهذه المصادر، وتطور الفقه والأدوار التي مر بها ومميزاته في كل دور والقسم الثاني يتناول النظريات الأساسية العامة نظرية الملكية وما يدخل تحتها من أسباب الملكية وتقسيم الملك وخصائص الملكية، ونظرية العقود وما يدخل تحتها من تكوين العقد والإرادة وشوائبها وآثار العقود والفسخ والبطلان وغير ذلك مما تتناوله عادة الكتب القانونية، ثم نظرية الأهلية والولاية .. إلخ وهكذا يسير الكتاب من
نظرية إلى نظرية فلا يترك نظرية حتى يوفيها حقها من البحث ويوفي ما يدخل تحتها من فروع حقها من البحث .
ومؤلف الكتاب لا ينسى أن يذكر بجوار المصطلح الإسلامي المصطلح القانوني ليبين الفرق بينهما في دقة التسمية، وليوسع بذلك معلومات القارىء، وينبه ذهنه إلى الموازنة والتعمق في الفهم.
والمؤلف الجليل الذي بذل هذا المجهود العظيم وأخرج هذا الكتاب الكريم هو الأستاذ الشيخ مصطفى أحمد الزرقا أستاذ الحقوق المدنية والشريعة الإسلامية في كلية الحقوق بدمشق
ولعل هذا التوفيق الذي لازم الشيخ في إخراج كتابه يرجع أولاً إلى حسن صلة الشيخ بالله ؛ فما يوفق هذا التوفيق إلا رجل يسدد الله خطاه، ثانياً إلى ما أفاء الله على الشيخ مصطفى من فضل الجمع بين دراسة ويرجع الشريعة الإسلامية والقوانين الوضعية. وكل ذلك ساعد الشيخ الزرقا على أن يحلق في هذا الأفق العالي، وأن يقدم للإسلام والمسلمين أجل الخدمات بهذا الكتاب القيم.
جزى الله الشيخ عن الإسلام والمسلمين خير الجزاء، ونفعنا بعلمه
وأمده بالقوة وكتب له التوفيق إنه سميع مجيب.
عبد القادر عودة
Preface by Professor Abd al-Qadir Awdah: Sweetness of paper, precise formatting, wonderful arrangement, linking branches to foundations, and a logical chain of theories and rulings. This book was the first of its kind missing from the Islamic library, and after its existence it is the first book upon which the Islamic jurisprudential renaissance will be built. The student of Islamic fiqh is in dire need of this book to know the foundations upon which fiqh stands, and so that some of these foundations become connected in his mind with others, and then he proceeds in his study with a correct direction. The most important thing about the book is that law students in the Islamic world can read it without feeling that they are reading something strange to them or far from them; rather, perhaps they will find in reading it such scientific pleasure, jurisprudential depth, and precision of linguistic and terminological expression that will make them prefer it over other law books that translate for them but do not author; indeed, perhaps they will find in it art and spirit that they have not found in any other book. The author, with ease and facility, through the strength of understanding and depth of fiqh that Allah has granted him, was able to present general Islamic theories as legal theories are presented, to connect each principle to its branches, and to extract from the branches their principles in his work on the Hanafi madhhab, although he balances in some issues between Islamic schools and does not forget in most cases to balance between the ruling of Sharia and Syrian laws. The book is arranged logically: the first part discusses fiqh and its sources, the historical order of these sources, the development of fiqh, the stages it went through, and its characteristics in each stage; the second part deals with fundamental general theories: the theory of ownership and what falls under it regarding causes of ownership, division of ownership, and characteristics of ownership; the theory of contracts and what falls under it regarding formation of contract, will and its defects, effects of contracts, rescission, invalidity, and other matters usually covered by legal books; then the theory of capacity and guardianship, etc. Thus the book proceeds from one theory to another, leaving no theory until it gives it its due of research and gives the branches under it their due of research. The author does not forget to mention alongside the Islamic term the legal term to show the difference between them in precision of nomenclature, and thereby to expand the reader's knowledge and alert his mind to comparison and depth of understanding. The venerable author who made this great effort and produced this noble book is Professor Sheikh Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, Professor of Civil Law and Islamic Sharia at the Faculty of Law in Damascus. Perhaps the success that accompanied the Sheikh in producing his book is due first to the Sheikh's good connection with Allah; for none is granted such success except a man whose steps Allah guides; secondly, to what Allah bestowed upon Sheikh Mustafa of the virtue of combining the study of Islamic Sharia and positive laws. All of this helped Sheikh al-Zarqa to soar to this high horizon and to present to Islam and Muslims the greatest services through this valuable book. May Allah reward the Sheikh for Islam and Muslims with the best reward, benefit us with his knowledge, strengthen him, and grant him success. Indeed, He is All-Hearing, All-Answering. Abd al-Qadir Awdah.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This is a preface written by Abd al-Qadir Awdah, a prominent scholar, praising Dr. Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa's monumental work 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm' (The General Introduction to Islamic Jurisprudence). The preface highlights the book's unique methodology: it treats Islamic legal theories in a systematic, logical manner similar to modern legal textbooks, yet rooted in classical Hanafi fiqh. It emphasizes the book's role in bridging Islamic jurisprudence with contemporary legal education, making it accessible to law students while maintaining depth and precision. Awdah notes the author's ability to present general theories (e.g., ownership, contracts, capacity) and link them to detailed branches, and also his comparative approach between Islamic schools and between Sharia and Syrian law. The preface serves as an endorsement of the book's value for the Islamic legal revival.

Key Terms
المدخل الفقهي العام (Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm): The General Introduction to Islamic Jurisprudence, a modern work by Mustafa al-Zarqa that systematically presents Hanafi legal theories.
نظرية الملكية (Nazariyyat al-Milkiyyah): Theory of ownership; a key general theory presented in the second part of the book.
نظرية العقود (Nazariyyat al-'Uqud): Theory of contracts; another major theory covering formation, defects, effects, rescission, and invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Significance of al-Zarqa's Foreword
Praise and introduction by 'Abd al-Qadir 'Auda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the methodological approach of Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa as presented in the foreword and identify its relevance for a Hanafi mufti.

Core Idea
Combining Islamic Shari'a and positive law enriches legal understanding and fatwa precision.

The foreword by 'Abd al-Qadir 'Auda introduces al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Am and highlights the unique methodology of its author, Shaykh Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. This lesson examines the key points in the foreword: al-Zarqa's thorough treatment of legal theories, his comparative approach between Islamic and positive legal terms, and his dual expertise. Understanding this methodological foundation is essential for appreciating how the book serves as a resource for Hanafi jurists navigating both classical fiqh and modern legal contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the foreword
Recognize that the foreword is a tribute to the author and his work, setting the stage for the book's significance.
Forewords often highlight the author's credentials and the book's unique contribution.
2
Analyze the methodology praised
Note the two key methodological features: (1) thorough exploration of each legal theory along with its sub-branches, and (2) comparison of Islamic terms with positive law equivalents to clarify nuances.
This comparative method is central to al-Madkhal's approach.
3
Examine the author's qualifications
Al-Zarqa is described as a professor of both civil law and Islamic Shari'a, enabling him to bridge the two fields. This dual expertise is a rare combination that enhances the book's authority.
The foreword links his success to piety and knowledge of both systems.
4
Connect to Hanafi iftaa practice
For a Hanafi mufti, understanding the relationship between classical fiqh and modern legal frameworks is increasingly important. Al-Zarqa's methodology offers tools for comparative analysis that can inform fatwa formulation.
The book equips the mufti with precise terminology and comparative insights.

Commentary
This passage is the opening foreword of the book, written by 'Abd al-Qadir 'Auda, a contemporary scholar. He praises the author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, for his comprehensive approach to legal theory, ensuring that each theory is thoroughly examined along with its branches. al-Zarqa is noted for his comparative method, juxtaposing Islamic legal terms with their positive law counterparts to clarify differences and deepen understanding. The foreword highlights al-Zarqa's unique qualification as a professor of both civil law and Islamic Shari'a, which enabled him to synthesize the two fields. The writer attributes the book's success to al-Zarqa's piety and his combined expertise in Islamic and secular law.

Key Terms
المصطلح الإسلامي (al-mustalah al-islami): Islamic legal term referring to concepts from Shari'a (e.g., riba, ijarah).
المصطلح القانوني (al-mustalah al-qanuni): Positive law term used in contemporary legal systems (e.g., interest, lease).
الموازنة (al-muwazanah): Comparison, aiming to balance and deepen understanding between two legal systems.

International Recognition of Islamic Sharia's Vitality
Introductory word citing international resolutions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key principles of the two international resolutions cited and evaluate their significance for the authority of Hanafi fiqh in modern fatwa.

Core Idea
International resolutions affirm Sharia's independent, living nature, supporting Hanafi fiqh's adaptability.

This passage from Dr. Munir al-Ajlani's preface to Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam presents two landmark international resolutions that explicitly recognize Islamic Sharia as a living, independent source of legislation. These resolutions, from 1937 and 1948, are not mere historical curiosities; they serve as authoritative external testimony to the resilience and relevance of Islamic jurisprudence. For the student of Hanafi fiqh and iftaa, understanding this recognition is crucial for appreciating how classical fiqh principles can engage with contemporary legal systems.

Guided Path
1
Identify the resolutions
Locate the two resolutions cited: the 1937 Congress of Comparative Law in The Hague and the 1948 International Bar Association. Note the key principles stated in each.
The first resolution contains three principles: Sharia as a source, living, and independent. The second calls for comparative study.
2
Analyze the implications
For each principle, consider how it relates to Hanafi usul and fatwa practice. For example, 'living and capable of evolution' aligns with the Hanafi concept of istihsan and custom.
These principles counter claims that Islamic law is static or derived from other systems.
3
Connect to the book's purpose
The book is an introduction to the Majallah (Ottoman civil code), which was based on Hanafi fiqh. The resolutions underscore the ongoing relevance of that project.
The Majallah itself is a modern codification of Hanafi law.
4
Reflect on contemporary fatwa
Consider how a mufti might use these resolutions as supporting evidence when addressing modern legal questions, while ensuring the ruling is rooted in Hanafi dalil.
The resolutions do not alter the primary sources but provide a contextual argument for Sharia's applicability.

كَلِمَة
بقلم : الدكتور منير العجلاني
المدخل الفقهي العام
(1)
يعد هذا الكتاب في نظرنا خير كتاب في التوطئة لدراسة مجلة الأحكام العدلية - القانون المدني العثماني القديم - وهو إلى ذلك دفاع مجيد عظمة الفقه الإسلامي، وقد نقل لنا مؤلفه ثلاثة نصوص دولية خطيرة عن تشيد بمزايا فقهنا ويسرنا أن نثبتها في هذه الكلمة:
القرار الأول : اتخذه مؤتمر الحقوق المقارنة المنعقد بمدينة لاهاي في
شهر آب من عام ١٩٣٧ وهو يتضمن ثلاثة مبادىء :
-
1
اعتبار الشريعة الإسلامية مصدراً من مصادر التشريع العام.
۲ - اعتبارها حية قابلة للتطور .
- اعتبارها تشريعاً قائماً بذاته ليس مأخوذاً من غيره .
ترجمته :
القرار الثاني : اتخذه مؤتمر المحامين الدولي عام ١٩٤٨ وهذه
يجب
اعترافاً بما في التشريع الإسلامي من مرونة وما له شأن، من على جمعية المحامين الدولية أن تقوم بتبني الدراسة المقارنة لهذا التشريع وبالتشجيع عليها».
A Word
By: Dr. Munir al-Ajlani
Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam (General Jurisprudential Introduction) (1)
This book in our view is the best book for introduction to the study of the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyyah - the old Ottoman civil code - and moreover it is a magnificent defense of the greatness of Islamic jurisprudence. The author has transmitted to us three serious international texts that praise the merits of our fiqh, and we are pleased to record them in this word:
The first resolution: Adopted by the Congress of Comparative Law held in The Hague in August 1937, and it includes three principles:
1- Considering Islamic Sharia as a source of general legislation.
2- Considering it living and capable of evolution.
3- Considering it as an independent legislation not derived from others.
Its translation:
The second resolution: Adopted by the International Bar Association in 1948, and it [states]: 'In recognition of the flexibility and importance of Islamic legislation, the International Bar Association must undertake to adopt the comparative study of this legislation and to encourage it.'
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is an introductory word by Dr. Munir al-Ajlani praising the book 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam'. He asserts it is the finest work for preparing to study the Majallah (the Ottoman civil code) and also serves as a powerful defense of the greatness of Islamic fiqh. He highlights that the author (Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa) recorded three significant international texts that commend Islamic jurisprudence. Al-Ajlani then reproduces two of these resolutions: the first from the 1937 Congress of Comparative Law in The Hague, which declares that Islamic Sharia is (1) a source of legislation, (2) living and capable of evolution, and (3) independent and not derived from other systems. The second resolution is from the 1948 International Bar Association, urging the study and encouragement of comparative research on Islamic legislation. These resolutions demonstrate external recognition of Islamic law's vitality and suitability for modern application, underscoring the relevance of the book's subject matter.

Key Terms
الشريعة الإسلامية (al-sharīʿa al-islāmiyya): Islamic divine law derived from Qur'an and Sunnah
مصادر التشريع (maṣādir al-tashrīʿ): Sources of legislation
قابل للتطور (qābil li-l-taṭawwur): Capable of evolution
المرونة (al-murūna): Flexibility

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is derived from Roman law.

Key Takeaway
International recognition of Sharia's independence and living nature reinforces the relevance of Hanafi fiqh for contemporary legal systems and fatwa.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Al-Zarqa's Modern Fiqh Methodology and Al-Ajlani's Critique
Foreword with praise and two methodological critiques

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Zarqa's methodological innovations in Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi and evaluate al-Ajlani's two criticisms regarding authoritative claims and textual interpretation.

Core Idea
A modern fiqh method must balance theoretical innovation with textual fidelity to avoid distorting sacred sources.

This foreword by Dr. Munir al-Ajlani offers both praise and pointed critique of Mustafa al-Zarqa's landmark work. While lauding al-Zarqa's synthesis of general juristic theories from diverse sources, al-Ajlani warns against two pitfalls: first, the reflexive claim that Islamic scholarship is always superior to Western thought, and second, the tendency to overburden scriptural texts to construct parallels with European legal doctrines. As a mufti or legal analyst, you must distinguish between legitimate theoretical development and forced interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Zarqa's key methodological shifts
Al-Zarqa moved away from case-based fiqh (fatwas and particulars) toward general theories (nazariyyat), synthesizing Qur'an, Hadith, and opinions from multiple schools to model civil law teaching in France.
His use of the Majallah as a springboard for theory-building, not just commentary.
2
Analyze the first critique: superiority claims
Al-Ajlani agrees that classical Islamic scholarship was superior to ancient Western thought, but warns against assuming contemporary Islamic thought always surpasses modern Western legal developments.
This touches on taqlid vs. ijtihad: blind praise impedes objective evaluation.
3
Analyze the second critique: overstretching texts
Al-Zarqa used Quran 4:29 (trade by mutual consent) to support the principle of autonomy of will. Al-Ajlani argues the verse does not imply that principle; it only prohibits wrongful consumption.
This is a classic naqd al-istidlal: the text’s dalalah (indication) does not match the claimed meaning.
4
Derive the methodological lesson for iftaa
When constructing general fiqh theories or applying qawaid, a mufti must ensure the textual evidence (dalil) genuinely supports the ruling, not be forced to fit a pre-existing Western framework.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that istinbat must be grounded in usul.

Source Text

كلمة الدكتور منير العجلاني
القرار الثالث : اتخذه مجمع الحقوق المقارنة الدولي المنعقد في باريس ١٩٥٢ وإليك ترجمته :
إن المؤتمرين بناء على الفائدة المتحققة من المباحث التي عرضت أثناء «أسبوع الفقه الإسلامي» وما جرى حولها من المناقشات التي تخلص منها بوضوح:
أ - أن مبادىء الفقه الإسلامي لها قيمة لا يمارى فيها.
ب - وأن اختلاف المذاهب الفقهية في هذه المجموعة الحقوقية العظمي ينطوي على ثروة من المفاهيم والمعلومات، ومن الأصول مناط الإعجاب وبها يتمكن الفقه الإسلامي أن يستجيب للحقوقية، وهي لجميع مطالب الحياة الحديثة والتوفيق بين حاجاتها.
يعلنون رغبتهم في أن يظل أسبوع الفقه الإسلامي) يتابع أعماله سنة فسنة ويكلفون مكتب المؤتمر وضع قائمة للموضوعات التي أظهرت . المناقشات ضرورة جعلها أساً للبحث في الدورة القادمة.
ويأمل المؤتمرون أن تؤلف لجنة لوضع معجم للفقه الإسلامي يسهل الرجوع إلى مؤلفات هذا الفقه فيكون معلمة فقهية تعرض فيها المعلومات الحقوقية الإسلامية وفقاً للأساليب الحديثة .
.. وكأن الأستاذ الزرقا قد استجاب لهذا الأمل، حين ألف كتاباً في الفقه الإسلامي على الأسلوب الحديث!
بدأ كتابه بتعريف الفقه الإسلامي، ثم ذكر مصادره الأولى الأربعة الأساسية : الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والقياس ومصادره التبعية: الاستحسان والمصالح المرسلة والعرف ثم بحث في أدوار أو أطوار) الفقه الإسلامي، فجعلها سبعة، أولها عصر النبوة، وآخرها عصر المجلة - ولسنا معه في هذا التقسيم، وإن يكن لعدد (٧) سره وسحره! - ثم دخل في صميم موضوعه، وهو : النظريات الفقهية الأساسية كنظريات الملك والعقد والأهلية إلخ.. لم ينسج فيها على منوال من سبقوه من شراح المجلة، الذين جعلوا الفقه «فتاوی» و «قضايا» و «جزئیات». وإنما حاول أن يدرس المجلة كما يدرس الأساتذة الفرنسيون في كلية الحقوق بباريس مادة القانون المدني، فجمع من أحكام القرآن والحديث وآراء الفقهاء من مختلف المذاهب، ما يؤلف نظريات عامة تشبه النظريات الأوروبية الحديثة، وقد وفق في محاولته توفيقاً كبيراً. فمن قرأ كتابه خرج منه بفائدتين النظريات الفقهية الجديدة، وله فضل إخراجها، وآراء الفقهاء التي لخصت للقارىء فأغنته عن قراءة عشرات من كتب الفقه.
وعلى إعجابنا بهذا الكتاب الجليل نشير إلى ناحية صغيرة ضعيفة منه كانت بمثابة «الخرزة الزرقاء . . أو التميمة من العين، وهذه الناحية هي أن الأستاذ الزرقاء ... يقول دائماً أن آراء علمائنا خير من آراء الغربيين، وأنا معه فقديمنا أفضل من قديمهم ولكن قديمنا ليس دائماً أفضل من جدیدهم!
هذه ملاحظة والملاحظة الثانية هي أن الأستاذ الزرقاء حمل بعض النصوص أكثر مما تستطيع أن تحمل في سبيل بناء نظريات عامة تشبه النظريات الغربية خذ لك مثلاً احتجاجه بالآية الكريمة: ﴿لَا تَأْكُلُوا أَمْوَالَكُم بَيْنَكُم بِالْبَاطِلِ إلا أن تكون تجرةٌ عَن تَراضِ مِنكُمْ (النساء: (٢٩/٤ لإثبات مبدأ سلطان الإرادة وليس في هذه الآية شيء من ذلك ! فمبدأ سلطان الإرادة أعلن تحرر الناس من المراسم والأشكال التي كانت تفقد المتعاقدين، في ظل الشريعة الرومانية القديمة، كثيراً من حريتهم وتفسد كثيراً من عقودهم وتعتبرها لغواً لمجرد أنها لم تستكمل بعض الشكليات» . . . فما الصلة بين هذا المبدأ والآية الكريمة؟
Statement by Dr. Munir al-Ajlani: The Third Resolution: Adopted by the International Court of Comparative Law held in Paris 1952. Here is its translation: The conferees, based on the benefit realized from the research presented during the 'Week of Islamic Fiqh' and the discussions that took place around it, which clearly concluded: A) That the principles of Islamic fiqh have undeniable value. B) That the differences among juristic schools in this great legal collection embody a wealth of concepts, information, and principles that are admirable, and through them Islamic fiqh can respond to all requirements of modern life and reconcile its needs. They announce their desire that the 'Week of Islamic Fiqh' continue its work year after year and charge the conference office to prepare a list of topics that the discussions have shown need to be made the basis for research in the next session. The conferees hope that a committee be formed to compile a dictionary of Islamic fiqh to facilitate reference to the works of this fiqh, making it a juristic encyclopedia presenting Islamic legal information according to modern methods. .. And it seems that Professor al-Zarqa responded to this hope when he wrote a book on Islamic fiqh in the modern style! He began his book with a definition of Islamic fiqh, then mentioned its four primary sources: the Book, the Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas), and its secondary sources: juristic preference (istihsan), public interest (masalih mursalah), and custom ('urf). Then he discussed the periods (or stages) of Islamic fiqh, making them seven, the first being the era of prophethood and the last being the era of al-Majallah - and we do not agree with him in this division, although the number seven has its charm! Then he entered the core of his subject: the fundamental juristic theories, such as the theories of ownership, contract, legal capacity, etc. He did not follow the pattern of his predecessors among the commentators of al-Majallah, who treated fiqh as 'fatwas', 'cases', and 'particulars'. Rather, he attempted to study al-Majallah as the French professors at the Faculty of Law in Paris teach civil law, gathering from the rulings of the Qur'an and Hadith and the opinions of jurists from various schools what constitutes general theories resembling modern European theories, and he succeeded greatly in his attempt. Whoever reads his book comes out with two benefits: the new juristic theories, and he has the merit of producing them; and the opinions of jurists that are summarized for the reader, sparing him the reading of dozens of books of fiqh. Despite our admiration for this great book, we point out a small weak aspect that is like a 'blue bead' or an amulet against the evil eye. This aspect is that Professor al-Zarqa always says that the opinions of our scholars are better than the opinions of Westerners. I agree with him that our old is better than their old, but our old is not always better than their new! This is one observation. The second observation is that Professor al-Zarqa burdens some texts more than they can bear in order to construct general theories resembling Western theories. Take, for example, his use of the noble verse: 'Do not consume your wealth among yourselves unjustly, unless it be a trade by mutual consent' (Quran 4:29) to prove the principle of autonomy of will, whereas there is nothing of that in this verse! The principle of autonomy of will declared the liberation of people from the formalities and forms that, under ancient Roman law, deprived contractors of much of their freedom and invalidated many of their contracts simply because they did not fulfill certain formalities... So what is the connection between this principle and the noble verse?
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a front matter written by Dr. Munir al-Ajlani, presenting his praise and critique of Mustafa al-Zarqa's book 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam'. The passage opens by quoting a 1952 resolution from the International Court of Comparative Law in Paris, which recognizes the value of Islamic fiqh and recommends ongoing study and the creation of a juristic dictionary. Al-Ajlani suggests that al-Zarqa's book responds to this call. He summarizes al-Zarqa's methodology: starting with a definition of fiqh, listing primary and secondary sources, dividing the history of fiqh into seven stages (a division al-Ajlani disagrees with but acknowledges the charm of the number seven), and then focusing on general theories like ownership, contract, and capacity. Unlike earlier commentators of the Majallah who focused on particulars, al-Zarqa treated the Majallah as European civil law is taught, synthesizing Qur'an, Hadith, and opinions from various schools into general theories. Al-Ajlani praises this as a great success, offering two benefits: new theories and a summary of juristic opinions. However, he offers two criticisms: (1) al-Zarqa always asserts that our scholars' views are superior to Western ones, but al-Ajlani counters that while our past is better than their past, it is not always better than their present. (2) al-Zarqa overstretches some texts to build general theories resembling Western ones, citing the example of using Q. 4:29 to support the principle of autonomy of will, which al-Ajlani argues is not supported by the verse.

Key Terms
الفقه الإسلامي (al-fiqh al-islami): Islamic jurisprudence, the body of legal rulings derived from the primary and secondary sources of Islam.
المجلة (al-Majallah): The Ottoman Civil Code (Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyyah), a codification of Hanafi fiqh rules in the 19th century.
النظريات الفقهية (al-nazariyyat al-fiqhiyyah): General juristic theories that unify multiple rulings under a coherent conceptual framework, such as theories of ownership, contract, and capacity.
سلطان الإرادة (sultan al-irada): The principle of autonomy of will, i.e., the freedom of parties to determine their contractual obligations without external formalities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is one of the two criticisms Dr. al-Ajlani makes about al-Zarqa's book?
A) That al-Zarqa ignored the Hanafi school entirely.
B) That al-Zarqa overstretched some religious texts to fit Western theories.
C) That al-Zarqa's division of fiqh history into seven stages is historically inaccurate.
D) That al-Zarqa focused too much on particular cases rather than general theories.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ajlani's foreword reminds muftis and jurists that theoretical innovation must be disciplined by textual fidelity, avoiding both reflexive triumphalism and forced interpretations.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Al-Zarqa's Fiqh Theories: Innovation and Methodological Critique
A critique of al-Zarqa's fiqh theoretical approach

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the strengths and weaknesses of Mustafa al-Zarqa's approach to constructing fiqh theories and identify proper vs. improper use of Quranic verses in deriving legal principles.

Core Idea
Building general fiqh theories is valuable, but must not overburden texts beyond their intended meaning.

Mustafa al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-`Amm revolutionized the study of Islamic law by presenting it as a system of theories comparable to modern legal frameworks. However, his method drew criticism for sometimes forcing Quranic verses to support Western legal concepts. This lesson examines both the achievement and the pitfalls.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Zarqa's method
Identify how al-Zarqa collected rulings from the Quran, hadith, and diverse juristic opinions to form general theories (e.g., theories of ownership, contract, capacity). This was a departure from traditional fiqh works that focused on fatwas and cases.
Al-Zarqa explicitly modeled his approach on French legal education.
2
Analyze the first critique: anachronistic preference
Al-Ajlani notes that al-Zarqa frequently claims Muslim classical opinions are superior to Western ones. While agreeing on the past, al-Ajlani argues that this does not always hold for modern developments.
This critique is about attitude, not fiqh content.
3
Analyze the second critique: over-interpretation of texts
Examine al-Ajlani's specific example: al-Zarqa uses Quran 4:29 (permission of trade by mutual consent) to prove the principle of autonomy of will (freedom from formalities). Al-Ajlani contends the verse says nothing about formalities; it simply prohibits injustice.
The verse's apparent meaning is limited to mutual consent; it does not establish a broad principle of party autonomy.
4
Evaluate proper istidlal
Consider how a Hanafi jurist should derive principles from such a verse. The proper method is to identify the 'illa (effective cause) and not to read modern concepts anachronistically. The Hanafi school recognizes freedom of contract through multiple sources, not a single proof-text.
This step highlights the importance of usul al-fiqh in preventing misuse of texts.

كلمة الدكتور منير العجلاني

يدرس التقسيم، وإن يكن لعدد (٧) سره وسحره! - ثم دخل في صميم موضوعه، وهو : النظريات الفقهية الأساسية كنظريات الملك والعقد والأهلية إلخ.. لم ينسج فيها على منوال من سبقوه من شراح المجلة، الذين جعلوا الفقه «فتاوی» و «قضايا» و «جزئیات». وإنما حاول أن يدرس المجلة كما الأساتذة الفرنسيون في كلية الحقوق بباريس مادة القانون المدني، فجمع من أحكام القرآن والحديث وآراء الفقهاء من مختلف المذاهب، ما يؤلف نظريات عامة تشبه النظريات الأوروبية الحديثة، وقد وفق في محاولته توفيقاً كبيراً. فمن قرأ كتابه خرج منه بفائدتين النظريات الفقهية الجديدة، وله فضل إخراجها، وآراء الفقهاء التي لخصت للقارىء فأغنته عن قراءة عشرات من كتب الفقه.
وعلى إعجابنا بهذا الكتاب الجليل نشير إلى ناحية صغيرة ضعيفة منه كانت بمثابة «الخرزة الزرقاء . . أو التميمة من العين، وهذه الناحية هي أن الأستاذ الزرقاء ... يقول دائماً أن آراء علمائنا خير من آراء الغربيين، وأنا معه فقديمنا أفضل من قديمهم ولكن قديمنا ليس دائماً أفضل من جديدهم!

وإن هاتين الملاحظتين لا تنقصان من قدر الكتاب الذي يستحق صاحبه أبلغ الثناء وأعظم التقدير وهو كتاب قوي بمادته، وصاحبه رجل متوقد الذكاء جمع بين الثقافتين الدينية والقانونية؛ قوي بلغته، فالأستاذ الزرقاء فقيه أديب، وأسلوبه في الكتابة يكاد ينسيك صعوبة المادة وجفافها . . .
الدكتور منير العجلاني
Word of Dr. Munir al-Ajlani

He studies the division, even if it is for the number (7) its secret and its magic! - Then he entered the core of his subject, which is: the fundamental fiqh theories such as theories of ownership, contract, legal capacity, etc. He did not follow the pattern of those before him among the commentators of the Majallah, who made fiqh into 'fatwas', 'cases', and 'particulars'. Rather, he tried to study the Majallah as the French professors at the Faculty of Law in Paris study the subject of civil law, so he collected from the rulings of the Qur'an and Hadith and the opinions of jurists from various schools, what constitutes general theories resembling modern European theories, and he succeeded greatly in his attempt. So whoever reads his book comes out with two benefits: the new fiqh theories (and he has the merit of producing them), and the opinions of the jurists which were summarized for the reader, making him independent of reading dozens of fiqh books.
Despite our admiration for this great book, we point out a small weak aspect that was like a 'blue bead... or amulet against the evil eye', and this aspect is that Professor al-Zarqa... always says that the opinions of our scholars are better than the opinions of Westerners, and I agree with him that our past is better than their past, but our past is not always better than their present!
This is one observation, and the second observation is that Professor al-Zarqa burdened some texts beyond what they can bear for the sake of building general theories resembling Western theories. Take for example his arguing with the noble verse: {Do not consume your wealth among yourselves unjustly unless it be a trade by mutual consent} (al-Nisa: 29) to prove the principle of autonomy of will, but there is nothing of that in this verse! For the principle of autonomy of will declared the liberation of people from the formalities and forms that used to deprive contractors in the shadow of ancient Roman law of much of their freedom and spoil many of their contracts and consider them void merely for not completing some formalities... So what is the connection between this principle and the noble verse?
Yet these two observations do not diminish the value of the book, which deserves the highest praise and greatest appreciation from its author. It is a book strong in its content, and its author is a man of brilliant intelligence who combined religious and legal culture; strong in his language, for Professor al-Zarqa is a jurist and a man of letters, and his style of writing almost makes you forget the difficulty and dryness of the subject...
Dr. Munir al-Ajlani
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a commendation (taqriz) by Dr. Munir al-Ajlani, a contemporary scholar, for Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa's book 'al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-`Amm'. The reviewer praises al-Zarqa's innovative approach: instead of merely compiling fatwas and details like previous commentators of the Majallah, al-Zarqa attempted to construct general fiqh theories (such as theories of ownership, contract, legal capacity) similar to those taught in French law schools. He drew from the Qur'an, Hadith, and opinions of jurists across schools, and succeeded in producing a work that offers both theoretical insights and a synthesis of classical fiqh opinions, saving the reader from consulting dozens of books.

However, Dr. al-Ajlani notes two criticisms. First, al-Zarqa routinely asserts that the opinions of classical Muslim scholars are superior to those of Westerners. While the reviewer agrees that the past of Muslims excels the past of the West, he argues that the classical Muslim heritage is not always better than modern Western thought. Second, al-Zarqa sometimes over-interprets scriptural texts to align with Western legal theories. As an example, the reviewer al-Ajlani points to al-Zarqa's citation of Quran 4:29 to support the principle of autonomy of will (sultan al-irada). The reviewer contends that this verse merely prohibits unjust consumption of property and requires mutual consent in trade; it does not establish the principle of autonomy of will as understood in Roman law, which abolished formalities. The reviewer questions the connection between the verse and that principle.

Despite these criticisms, the reviewer reaffirms the book's great value and lauds al-Zarqa as a brilliant scholar combining religious and legal knowledge, with a literary style that alleviates the dryness of the subject.

Key Terms
النظريات الفقهية (al-nazariyyat al-fiqhiyyah): General theoretical frameworks derived from fiqh rulings, similar to legal theories in modern law (e.g., theory of ownership, contract, capacity).
مبدأ سلطان الإرادة (mabda' sultan al-iradah): The principle that parties are free to contract without being bound by formalities; their will alone suffices.
إستدلال (istidlal): The process of deriving legal rulings from sources; here, the critique focuses on flawed istidlal by reading modern concepts into classical texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Dr. al-Ajlani's critique, what is the main problem with al-Zarqa's use of Quran 4:29 to support the principle of autonomy of will?
A) The verse is abrogated by later revelation.
B) The verse does not mention autonomy of will; it only prohibits injustice and requires mutual consent.
C) The verse only applies to written contracts.
D) The principle of autonomy of will is already established in the earlier verse 2:282.

Key Takeaway
Al-Zarqa's innovative systematization of fiqh into theories is praiseworthy, but his method of over-interpreting verses to align with modern concepts is a methodological flaw that must be avoided in proper Hanafi istidlal.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Structure and Purpose of Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm
Preface outlining book structure and history

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three main sections of Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm and explain how the book serves as an introduction to the principles, theories, and universal maxims of Islamic jurisprudence.

Core Idea
Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm introduces fiqh principles, not specific rulings.

This preface by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa introduces his seminal work, 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm', which serves as a comprehensive introduction to Islamic jurisprudence. The author explains that the book is divided into three parts: a historical and introductory section on the sources and development of fiqh, a presentation of the fundamental jurisprudential theories underlying legal rulings, and an exposition of the universal legal maxims (al-qawa'id al-kulliyya) with brief commentary. This structure reflects his pedagogical approach, developed through years of university teaching, to provide students with a systematic understanding of the foundations of fiqh before delving into specific rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's purpose
Understand that this is an introductory text (madkhal) aiming to equip students with the foundational knowledge needed to study fiqh systematically. It is not a collection of rulings but a framework for understanding how rulings are derived.
Note the term 'madkhal' meaning 'introduction'.
2
List the three main sections
Extract from the text: (1) an introductory historical preface on sources and development of fiqh, (2) a presentation of basic jurisprudential theories (al-nazariyyat al-fiqhiyya al-asasiyya) concerning the foundations of rulings, and (3) an exposition of the universal maxims (al-qawa'id al-kulliyya) with brief explanation.
These sections are the backbone of the book.
3
Note the author's pedagogical context
Recognize that the book originated from university teaching, with the author writing and distributing fascicles to students from 1944. The fourth edition expanded to two volumes for the first two years of study. This context explains the book's structured, progressive approach.
The author revised based on teaching experience.
4
Recognize the importance of universal maxims
The third section on al-qawa'id al-kulliyya is especially relevant for the discipline of iftaa (issuing legal opinions). These maxims, such as 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha', are overarching principles that help a mufti derive rulings in new cases (nawazil).
In Hanafi usul, these maxims are collected in works like al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir.

الحمد لله الذي أتم علينا نعمته والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد رسول الهدى وعلى من بسنته اهتدى وعلى وصحبه .
وبعد فقد بني هذا المدخل الفقهي العام على ثلاثة أقسام هي: مقدمة تعريفية وتاريخية عن مصادر الفقه وأدوار تطوره، ويليها عرض للنظريات الفقهية الأساسية في مباني الأحكام ثم بيان للقواعد الكلية في الفقه
مع شرح موجز لها . وقد دعتني حاجة التدريس الجامعي إلى أن أقوم بتدريس هذا المدخل وكتابته وطبع ما أكتبه بالتتابع كراريس متفرقة في وقت واحد لتوزيعها على الطلاب منذ عام ١٣٦٣هـ = ١٩٤٤م. ثم كنت أزيد في كل طبعة لاحقة وأنقح بحسب ما تظهره لي حاجة التدريس الجامعي. وفي الطبعة الرابعة أصبح هذا المدخل الفقهي العام جزءين اثنين موزعاً تدريسهما على السنتين الجامعيتين الأولى والثانية. وتتابعت طبعاته حتى الطبعة الثامنة المنقحة حين تقاعدت من جامعة دمشق بحكم بلوغي السن القانونية في آخر عام ١٩٦٦م. واستمر تدريس المدخل في الجامعة بعدي بضع سنين صدرت خلالها طبعات جديدة حصل فيها أخطاء مطبعية كثيرة . ثم توقف تدريسه في جامعة
Praise be to Allah who has perfected His grace upon us, and blessings and peace be upon our master Muhammad, the Messenger of guidance, and upon those who follow his Sunnah, and upon his Companions.
After: This general jurisprudential introduction is built upon three sections: an introductory and historical preface on the sources of fiqh and the stages of its development, followed by a presentation of the fundamental jurisprudential theories concerning the foundations of rulings, then an exposition of the universal maxims in fiqh with a brief explanation of them. The need for university teaching prompted me to teach this introduction, write it, and print what I wrote in sequence as separate fascicles at one time for distribution to students starting from 1363 AH = 1944 AD. Then I would add and revise in each subsequent edition according to what the need for university teaching showed me. In the fourth edition, this general jurisprudential introduction became two parts, with its teaching distributed over the first and second university years. Its editions continued up to the eighth revised edition when I retired from the University of Damascus due to reaching the legal age at the end of 1966 AD. The teaching of the introduction continued at the university after me for a few years during which new editions were published that contained many typographical errors. Then its teaching stopped at the university.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to the new edition of the series 'Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garb', which begins with 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm'. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, outlines the structure of the book: first, an introductory and historical section on the sources of fiqh and its development; second, a presentation of the basic jurisprudential theories regarding the foundations of legal rulings; and third, an exposition of the universal legal maxims with brief commentary. He then recounts the book's history, starting from his teaching at the university, where he wrote and distributed fascicles, through multiple editions, and finally his retirement and the subsequent typographical errors in later editions. This front matter gives the student insight into the work's organization and the author's pedagogical approach.

Key Terms
القواعد الكلية في الفقه (al-Qawa'id al-Kulliyya fi al-Fiqh): The universal legal maxims that are overarching principles applied across various chapters of fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A presentation of the fundamental jurisprudential theories concerning the foundations of rulings.
C) An exposition of the universal maxims in fiqh with brief explanation.
D) A detailed analysis of the differences between the four Sunni schools of law.

Key Takeaway
Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm is a structured introduction to fiqh, focusing on history, theory, and universal maxims, designed for university-level pedagogical progression.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Methodological Approach of Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm
Author's biographical and methodological introduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the methodological innovation of presenting fiqh in modern legal formulation and identify the three-part structure of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm.

Core Idea
The book presents fiqh in modern legal language while preserving its essence.

In this introduction, the author outlines the structure of his work and narrates its development. He emphasizes that the key innovation is the use of modern legal formulation to make fiqh accessible to students without traditional Sharia training, while maintaining the original rulings. This lesson will explore that methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Sections
The author states the book is built on three sections: a definitional and historical introduction about fiqh sources and development, a presentation of fundamental juristic theories concerning the foundations of rulings, and an exposition of universal maxims with brief explanations. Extract these three from the text.
These correspond to the standard divisions of a legal introduction: history, theory, and maxims.
2
Trace the Book's Evolution
The author describes writing and printing the book in serial notebooks starting in 1363 AH (1944 AD), then revising through eight editions until retirement in 1966. Note how the fourth edition split into two parts for two university years.
This shows the book's development in response to teaching needs.
3
Recognize the Methodological Shift
The book originally explained the Ottoman Majallah, then adapted to the Syrian Civil Code. The author decided to formulate fiqh rulings in the style of modern legal language (the 'new garment') while preserving the rulings' essence. Identify the key phrase: 'preserving the original rulings and juristic views in their essence and core'.
This balance between form and substance is the core methodological contribution.
4
Assess the Impact
The author claims this new approach received wide acceptance and became the common method. Consider why this approach was necessary: to address students without Sharia background and meet contemporary university study needs.
The approach is still relevant today in legal education and fatwa drafting.
