الله الحر الحيمة [؟]
مقدمة هذا الإخراج الجديد لسلسلة: الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد وفي طليعتها المدخل الفقهي العام
الحمد لله الذي أتم علينا نعمته والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد رسول الهدى وعلى من بسنته اهتدى وعلى وصحبه .
وبعد فقد بني هذا المدخل الفقهي العام على ثلاثة أقسام هي: مقدمة تعريفية وتاريخية عن مصادر الفقه وأدوار تطوره، ويليها عرض للنظريات الفقهية الأساسية في مباني الأحكام ثم بيان للقواعد الكلية في الفقه مع شرح موجز لها . وقد دعتني حاجة التدريس الجامعي إلى أن أقوم بتدريس هذا المدخل وكتابته وطبع ما أكتبه بالتتابع كراريس متفرقة في وقت واحد لتوزيعها على الطلاب منذ عام ١٣٦٣هـ = ثم كنت أزيد في كل طبعة لاحقة وأنقح بحسب ما تظهره لي حاجة التدريس الجامعي. وفي الطبعة الرابعة أصبح هذا المدخل الفقهي العام جزءين اثنين موزعاً تدريسهما على السنتين الجامعيتين الأولى والثانية. وتتابعت طبعاته حتى الطبعة الثامنة المنقحة حين تقاعدت من جامعة دمشق بحكم بلوغي السن القانونية في آخر عام ١٩٦٦م. واستمر تدريس المدخل في الجامعة بعدي بضع سنين صدرت خلالها طبعات جديدة حصل فيها أخطاء مطبعية كثيرة . ثم توقف تدريسه في جامعة دمشق، وكل ما صدر له بعد ذلك كان طبعات مسروقة غير مأذونة حتى يومنا هذا، وكثيرة الأخطاء المطبعية .
وقد تراكم لدي بعد صدور الطبعة الثامنة وخلال تدريسي لهذا المدخل في كلية الشريعة بالجامعة الأردنية منذ أوائل السبعينيات، تصحيحات أخطاء وتنقيحات وإضافات مناسبة أدخلتها جميعاً في هذا الإخراج الجديد الآن.
صدرت الطبعات الأولى لهذا المدخل ونحن حينئذ في ظل مجلة الأحكام العدلية التي كانت بمثابة القانون المدني في الدولة العثمانية، وكان هذا الكتاب مدخلاً إلى الفقه الإسلامي عامة، وإلى مجلة الأحكام العدلية خاصة .
الأجنبي
ثم صدر القانون المدني السوري المستمد من أصول الفقه القانوني في أواخر عام ١٩٤٩م، وتوليت أنا تدريسه أيضاً بدل مجلة الأحكام العدلية.
واستمرينا في تدريس المدخل الفقهي تحت عنوان مادة الشريعة الإسلامية . ومن فضل الله وتوفيقه أن المدخل شق في صياغة الفقه وتدريسه في الجامعات طريقاً لم يكن معهوداً قبله وأن هذا النهج الجديد في تقديم الفقه الإسلامي للطلاب غير ذوي الخلفية الشرعية لقي قبولاً واسعاً حتى صار هو الطريقة الشائعة. ويقوم هذا النهج الذي اعتزمت اتباعه منذئذ في سلسلة (الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد) على صوغ الأحكام الفقهية التي تشرح مجلة الأحكام العدلية كصياغة الفقه القانوني الحديث، ليلبس الفقه الإسلامي بذلك ثوباً جديداً يتفق مع الأذواق القانونية المعاصرة في صياغته ومظهره، ويحافظ في الأحكام والأنظار الفقهية على أصله وجوهره. وهذا ما تقتضيه الدراسة الجامعية وحاجة العصر. ومما كتبته عن الصياغة الجديدة لهذا الكتاب في مقدمتي للجزء الثالث للسلسلة في عام ١٣٦٥هـ (١٩٤٦م) : إني أعلم ما في هذه الخطوة من خطورة ومن جهود عظيمة، فإن الفقه القانوني والقوانين الحديثة المنشأة على أساسه تسير من الأصول
Introduction to this new edition of the series: Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garment, and at its forefront is the General Introduction to Islamic Jurisprudence. Praise be to God who has completed His favor upon us, and peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad, the Messenger of guidance, and upon whoever follows his Sunnah, and upon his Companions. To proceed: This General Introduction to Islamic Jurisprudence is built upon three sections: a definitional and historical introduction about the sources of fiqh and its stages of development, followed by a presentation of the fundamental juristic theories concerning the foundations of rulings, then an exposition of the universal maxims in fiqh with a brief explanation of them. The need for university teaching prompted me to teach this introduction and write it and print what I wrote in successive separate notebooks at the same time for distribution to students since 1363 AH (1944 AD). Then I kept adding to each subsequent edition and revising according to what the need of university teaching showed me. In the fourth edition, this General Introduction became two parts, distributed for teaching over the first and second university years. Its editions continued until the eighth revised edition when I retired from the University of Damascus due to reaching the legal age at the end of 1966 AD. The teaching of the Introduction continued in the university after me for a few years, during which new editions were published that contained many typographical errors. Then its teaching stopped at the University of Damascus, and everything published thereafter was unauthorized pirated editions until this day, with many typographical errors. I have accumulated after the publication of the eighth edition and during my teaching of this Introduction at the College of Sharia at the University of Jordan since the early seventies, corrections of errors, revisions, and appropriate additions, all of which I have incorporated into this new edition now. The first editions of this Introduction were published while we were under the shadow of the Majallat al-Ahkam al-Adliyya, which served as the civil code in the Ottoman Empire, and this book was an introduction to Islamic fiqh in general, and to the Majallat al-Ahkam al-Adliyya in particular. Foreign. Then the Syrian Civil Code, derived from the principles of legal jurisprudence, was issued at the end of 1949 AD, and I undertook its teaching as well instead of the Majallat al-Ahkam al-Adliyya. We continued teaching the General Introduction under the title Islamic Sharia course. By God's grace and success, the Introduction opened a path in the formulation and teaching of fiqh in universities that was not customary before it, and this new approach in presenting Islamic fiqh to students without a Sharia background received wide acceptance until it became the common method. This approach, which I decided to follow since then in the series (Islamic Jurisprudence in Its New Garment), is based on formulating the fiqh rulings that explain the Majallat al-Ahkam al-Adliyya in the style of modern legal formulation, so that Islamic fiqh wears a new garment that agrees with contemporary legal tastes in its formulation and appearance, while preserving the original rulings and juristic views in their essence and core. This is what university study and the need of the age require. And among what I wrote about the new formulation of this book in my introduction to the third part of the series in 1365 AH (1946 AD): I know the gravity of this step and the tremendous efforts required, for legal jurisprudence and the modern laws established upon its basis proceed from the principles.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the new edition of his book. He begins by outlining the three-part structure of the work: a historical introduction to fiqh sources, a presentation of fundamental juristic theories, and an exposition of universal legal maxims. He then narrates the book's development over decades, from its initial serial publication for university students in 1944 to the eighth edition in 1966. He explains how the book was originally written to explain the Ottoman Majallah and later adapted when the Syrian Civil Code replaced it. The key methodological innovation is the deliberate use of modern legal language and formulation to make Islamic fiqh accessible to law students without traditional Sharia training, while preserving the substance of the rulings. This approach gained wide acceptance and became standard. The author emphasizes that this new garment changes only the presentation, not the essence of fiqh.

Key Terms
المدخل الفقهي العام (al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm): The title of this textbook, structured in three sections: a historical introduction to fiqh sources, a presentation of fundamental juristic theories, and an exposition of universal maxims with brief explanations.
مجلة الأحكام العدلية (Majallat al-Ahkam al-Adliyya): The civil code of the Ottoman Empire, which this book originally aimed to explain.
الفقه الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد (al-Fiqh al-Islami fi Thawbihi al-Jadid): The series to which this book belongs, characterized by presenting Islamic fiqh in modern legal formulation.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Author's Methodological Shift: From Branches to Principles
Author explains his methodological innovation and the book's pedagogical purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between traditional fiqh methodology and modern legal fiqh methodology, and identify how Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam implements the latter.

Core Idea
Traditional fiqh proceeds from branches; modern legal fiqh proceeds from principles.

This passage from Mustafa al-Zarqa's introduction explains why his book Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam is not a traditional fiqh text. He contrasts the methodology of the Majallat and classical fiqh—which deal directly with branches and scatter principles—with the modern legal approach of starting from general principles and deriving specific rulings. Al-Zarqa chose the latter to make Islamic fiqh accessible to university students without a sharia background.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methodologies
Find the description of the traditional approach (branches first, principles scattered) and the modern legal approach (principles first, branches derived).
The key phrase is 'يسير بعكس ذلك' indicating the reversal.
2
Understand the traditional approach
Classical fiqh and Majallat treat branches directly, scattering principles along the way as occasions arise.
This is 'عالج الفروع مباشرة'.
3
Understand the modern legal approach
Modern legal fiqh starts with general principles and moves to specific branches derived from those principles.
This is 'تسير من الأصول والمبادئ العامة...إلى فروع الأحكام'.
4
Recognize al-Zarqa's choice
Al-Zarqa adopted the modern approach for his series 'Islamic Fiqh in its New Garment' to suit contemporary legal tastes and university education.
He aimed to 'يلبس الفقه الإسلامي ثوباً جديداً' while preserving the essence.
5
Identify the book's educational purpose
The book is an introductory text teaching basic concepts and methodology, not a detailed reference. Examples serve pedagogical goals.
Al-Zarqa resisted turning it into an encyclopedia of rulings.

مقدمة الإخراج الجديد للمدخل الفقهي العام

والمبادىء العامة بترتيب خاص، إلى فروع الأحكام الجزئية التي تقوم على أساس تلك المبادىء العامة أو تستثنى منها وفقهنا - ومنه مجلة الأحكام العدلية - يسير بعكس ذلك، فيعالج الفروع مباشرة، وينثر أجزاء المبادىء العامة والأصول الكلية في طريقه بحسب المناسبات.
فجمع أجزاء هذه المبادىء العامة من مختلف الأبواب، واستيحاؤها غالباً من فروع الأحكام وعللها، ثم ضم كل جزء إلى أخيه ليستخلص من كل مجموعة منها الأصل الشرعي الذي يحكم فيها وتردّ الفروع إليه، كل يستدعي من الجهد والوقت ما يجب أن يتعاون عليه جماعة من فقهاء الشريعة والقانون ينصرفون بكل مواهبهم إليه».

إن هذا الإخراج الجديد الآن للكتاب بعد جميع طبعاته السابقة - يتميز في الشكل وفي المضمون.
·
(أ) - ففي المضمون، حرصت على التمسك بالطابع والأسلوب التعليمي لهذا الكتاب ليبقى موطاً لطلاب كليات الشريعة والحقوق القادمين من الثانوية العامة ممن ليست لهم خلفية شرعية وقاومت كل إغراء بتحويل الكتاب إلى موسوعة للأحكام الفقهية أو الفتاوى أو مرجع متعمق لدقائق الفقه وتفاصيله فما زال الكتاب الآن كما أردت له أصلاً أن يكون مدخلاً موطاً يعلم الطالب الجامعي المفاهيم الفقهية الأساسية ومنهج التفكير الفقهي السديد وليس تفاصيل وفروع الأحكام الفقهية التي تعج بها كتب الفقه التقليدية وما يتضمنه الكتاب من أحكام فقهية هدفه الأساسي هو خدمة غرضه التعليمي بضرب الأمثلة وإيراد الشواهد وتشخيص المفاهيم المجردة، وتثبيت القضايا الرئيسية في ذهن الطالب. وقد زدت عدد الأمثلة الإيضاحية المختارة بعناية لتناسب حاجة المبتدىء في التوضيح.
ثم قد استحدثت الآن في هذا الإخراج الجديد، في أواخر بعض الفصول، ملحقات صغت فيها القضايا والمسائل التفصيلية والمتعمقة التي
١٧
Introduction to the new edition of Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam. Damascus, and everything published after that was stolen unauthorized editions until this day, with many typographical errors. After the eighth edition and during my teaching of this Madkhal at the College of Sharia at the University of Jordan since the early seventies, corrections of errors, revisions, and appropriate additions have accumulated, all of which I have included in this new edition now. The first editions of this Madkhal were published while we were under the shadow of the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya, which served as the civil code in the Ottoman Empire, and this book was an introduction to Islamic fiqh in general, and to the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya in particular. Then the Syrian Civil Code derived from the principles of legal fiqh was issued in late 1949, and I also undertook its teaching instead of the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya. And we continued teaching the Madkhal fiqhi under the title of the subject 'Islamic Sharia'. And by God's grace and assistance, the Madkhal opened a path in the formulation and teaching of fiqh in universities that was not customary before it, and this new approach in presenting Islamic fiqh to students without a sharia background gained wide acceptance until it became the common method. This approach, which I intended to follow since then in the series 'Islamic Fiqh in its New Garment', is based on formulating the fiqh rulings that explain the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya as a formulation of modern legal fiqh, so that Islamic fiqh wears a new garment that agrees with contemporary legal tastes in its formulation and appearance, while preserving its origin and essence in rulings and juristic considerations. This is what university study and the need of the age require. And among what I wrote about the new formulation of this book in my introduction to the third part of the series in 1365 AH (1946 CE): 'I know the gravity and great effort in this step, for legal fiqh and modern laws based on it proceed from general principles and foundations in a specific order to the branches of partial rulings that are based on those general principles or excepted from them. But our fiqh—and from it the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya—proceeds conversely, dealing directly with branches, and scattering parts of general principles and universal foundations along its way according to occasions. So collecting the parts of these general principles from various chapters, deriving them often from the branches of rulings and their underlying reasons, then joining each part to its counterpart to extract from each group the sharia principle that governs them and to which the branches are referred—all this demands effort and time that a group of sharia and legal scholars must cooperate with all their talents.' That is so. Indeed, this new edition of the book after all its previous editions is distinguished in form and content. (A) In content: I was keen to adhere to the educational character and style of this book so that it remains a prepared text for students of sharia and law colleges coming from general secondary school who have no sharia background, and I resisted every temptation to transform the book into an encyclopedia of fiqh rulings or fatwas or a deep reference for the subtleties and details of fiqh. So the book remains now as I originally intended it to be: a prepared introduction that teaches the university student the basic fiqh concepts and the proper method of fiqh thinking, not the details and branches of fiqh rulings that crowd traditional fiqh books. And the fiqh rulings that the book contains have as their primary goal serving its educational purpose by providing examples, presenting evidence, personifying abstract concepts, and fixing the main issues in the student's mind. I have increased the number of carefully chosen explanatory examples to suit the beginner's need for clarification. Then I have now introduced in this new edition, at the end of some chapters, appendices in which I have formulated the detailed and in-depth issues and topics that... (page 17 cut off)
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the new edition of his book 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam' (The General Legal Introduction). It is a front matter passage that outlines the history, methodology, and distinctive features of this edition. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, explains that the first editions were published during the era of the Ottoman civil code (Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya), and the book served as an introduction to Islamic fiqh in general and to that code in particular. After the Syrian Civil Code was enacted in 1949, the author taught it instead, but continued teaching the Madkhal under the title 'Islamic Sharia'. He highlights that his approach, first presented in his series 'Islamic Fiqh in its New Garment', was innovative: he formulated fiqh rulings in the style of modern legal codes, making them accessible to students without a traditional sharia background. This approach – moving from general principles to specific branches, rather than the traditional method of dealing with branches directly – gained wide acceptance. In this new edition, he has corrected errors, added revisions, and increased the number of explanatory examples. He emphasizes that the book remains an introductory textbook, not an encyclopedia of detailed rulings. Its purpose is to teach fundamental concepts and the correct method of juristic thinking, using examples and evidence. He has also added appendices with more detailed topics at the end of some chapters.

Key Terms
مجلة الأحكام العدلية (Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya): The Ottoman civil code that codified Hanafi fiqh principles, serving as a reference for this book.
الفقه القانوني (al-fiqh al-qanuni): Legal jurisprudence as understood in modern law, emphasizing systematic formulation from general principles to specific rules.
المدخل الفقهي (al-madkhal al-fiqhi): A foundational introductory textbook that teaches basic fiqh concepts and methodology, not detailed rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of the book 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam' according to its author?
A) To serve as a comprehensive reference for fatwas.
B) To teach university students basic fiqh concepts and the proper method of fiqh thinking.
C) To replace the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya entirely.
D) To provide a deep analysis of detailed fiqh rulings.

Key Takeaway
Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam adopts the modern legal methodology of proceeding from general principles to specific rulings, for pedagogical purposes, and remains an introductory textbook, not a reference work.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Methodological Approach of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm
Author explains methodological contrast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the contrasting methodological approaches of traditional fiqh works and al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm.

Core Idea
Al-Madkhal gathers general principles from rulings, unlike traditional works that scatter principles among branches.

The preface to the new edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm presents a clear methodological vision. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, explains that his book takes a different path from traditional fiqh works: instead of starting from detailed rulings and scattering general principles along the way, it systematically collects general principles from various chapters and uses rulings as illustrative examples. This approach makes the book a preparatory text for beginners, teaching fundamental concepts and methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two approaches
The author contrasts traditional fiqh works (including the Majalla) that directly treat branches (furu‘) and only mention principles incidentally, with his own approach that gathers general principles from different chapters and uses branches to exemplify them.
Key contrast: principles versus branches as the starting point.
2
Understand the goal of each approach
Traditional works aim for comprehensive coverage of rulings, while al-Madkhal aims to teach fundamentals and methodology, using rulings as teaching tools.
This difference is crucial for the book's educational purpose.
3
Note the collaborative challenge
The author states that extracting principles from branches and organizing them requires collective effort from jurists and legal scholars.
Highlights the synthetic nature of the project.
4
Apply the distinction to your own study
When using al-Madkhal, focus on the principles and reasoning, not just the detailed rulings, which serve to illustrate principles.
Aligns with the book's preparatory nature.

فجمع أجزاء هذه المبادىء العامة من مختلف الأبواب، واستيحاؤها غالباً من فروع الأحكام وعللها، ثم ضم كل جزء إلى أخيه ليستخلص من كل مجموعة منها الأصل الشرعي الذي يحكم فيها وتردّ الفروع إليه، كل يستدعي من الجهد والوقت ما يجب أن يتعاون عليه جماعة من فقهاء الشريعة والقانون ينصرفون بكل مواهبهم إليه».

ثم قد استحدثت الآن في هذا الإخراج الجديد، في أواخر بعض الفصول، ملحقات صغت فيها القضايا والمسائل التفصيلية والمتعمقة التي
تتعدى حاجة المبتدىء، لكنها تنفع الطالب المتقدم والمراجع الذي يريد التوسع والأصل في هذه الملحقات أنها تتجاوز حاجة الطلاب في مرحلة الإجازة (البكالوريوس) فلا تطلب منهم دراسة وامتحاناً. وبعض هذه الملحقات كان في الأصل حواشي مطولة في ثنايا الفصول، أما ما بقي من حواشي متعمقة لكنها لقصرها لا تستحق أن تفرد في ملحق، فحافظت على بقائها في أماكنها مع تمييزها بنجم ( ) ليتعداها الطالب دون حرج ويعلم. أنها ليست مطلوبة منه في الامتحانات.
كما عنيت في هذا الإخراج الجديد بتقريب المدخل - قدر ما يسمح به طابعه التعليمي - من الواقع المعاصر وقضاياه. فالفقه الإسلامي ليس تراثاً نضعه في المتحف وننفض عنه الغبار لنعرضه على الزوار، بل هو فهم للشريعة الإلهية التي ارتضاها الله للناس ليهتدوا بها في حياتهم العملية ويهدوا إليها الإنسانية. ومما أضيف إلى المدخل لهذا الغرض الآن : فصل جديد عن مميزات الدور الفقهي (الثامن) الذي نعيشه اليوم، وكذلك ملاحق متعددة تناولت فيما تناولته : حكم الفوائد المصرفية وسلطة ولي الأمر، والسياسة الشرعية، وتقنين الفقه والتقنين منه، وتوحيد التشريع في البلاد العربية وعقوبة الزنى والفرق بين مدرستي أهل الحديث وأهل الرأي (وهذه قضية قديمة تثور حولها تساؤلات معاصرة). أما الفهرس الهجائي التفصيلي للموضوعات والأعلام فقد جدد تجديداً
كاملاً حيث تفاقم في الطبعات السابقة الخلل فيه.

ب - أما في الشكل : فبحسب هذا التقسيم الجديد تتتابع الفصول في المدخل الفقهي العام كله بالتسلسل من الفصل الأول إلى الأخير، دون أن يتكرر رقم أي فصل: فالباب الأول مثلاً يشمل الفصلين الأول والثاني ويليه الباب الثاني الذي يبدأ بالفصل الثالث وينتهي بالفصل الثامن، ليبدأ بعده الباب الثالث من الفصل التاسع وهكذا.
Preface to the new edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm
·
And general principles in a special order, to the branches of detailed rulings that are based on those general principles or are excepted from them. Our jurisprudence - including the Majalla al-Ahkam al-Adliyya - proceeds in the opposite manner: it directly deals with branches, and scatters parts of general principles and universal maxims along the way as appropriate. Gathering the parts of these general principles from various chapters, deriving them mostly from branches of rulings and their causes (illal), then joining each part to its counterpart to extract from each group the legal principle (asl shar‘i) that governs them and to which the branches are referred—all of this requires effort and time that should be undertaken cooperatively by a group of jurists and legal scholars dedicating all their talents to it.
...
Indeed, this new edition of the book after all its previous editions is distinguished in form and content.
·
(A) Content-wise: I have adhered to the educational character and style of this book so that it remains a preparatory text for students of Shari‘a and law colleges coming from general secondary education who have no religious background, and I resisted all temptation to turn the book into an encyclopedia of fiqh rulings or fatwas or an advanced reference for the minutiae and details of fiqh. Thus the book remains, as I originally intended it to be, an introductory preparatory text that teaches the university student the basic fiqh concepts and the sound method of fiqh thinking, not the details and branches of fiqh rulings found in traditional fiqh books. The fiqh rulings it contains serve primarily its educational purpose by providing examples, citing evidence, concretizing abstract concepts, and fixing the main issues in the student's mind. I have increased the number of carefully chosen illustrative examples to suit the need of the beginner for clarification.
Moreover, in this new edition I have introduced appendices at the end of some chapters, in which I have formulated detailed and advanced issues and questions that exceed the beginner's need but benefit the advanced student and the researcher who seeks expansion. The principle regarding these appendices is that they go beyond the need of students at the bachelor's level, so they are not required for study or examination. Some of these appendices originally were lengthy footnotes within the chapters; as for the remaining advanced footnotes that are too short to be detached as appendices, I kept them in their places, marked with a star (*) so that the student can bypass them without hesitation and know that they are not required in exams.
In this new edition I also aimed to bring the introduction as close as possible—to the extent permitted by its educational character—to contemporary reality and its issues. Islamic jurisprudence is not a heritage to be placed in a museum and dusted off for visitors; it is an understanding of the divine Shari‘a that Allah has chosen for people to be guided by in their practical life and to guide humanity thereby. Among what I have added to this introduction for this purpose now: a new chapter on the characteristics of the eighth fiqh period in which we live today, as well as various appendices that address among other things: the ruling on bank interest and the authority of the guardian (wali al-amr), siyasa shar‘iyya, codification of fiqh and its codification, unification of legislation in Arab countries, the punishment for zina, and the difference between the schools of hadith and ra’y (an old issue around which contemporary questions arise). As for the detailed alphabetical index of topics and prominent figures, it has been completely renewed because the previous editions suffered from increasing defects.
-
(B) Form-wise: According to this new division, the chapters in the entire al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm are arranged consecutively from the first chapter to the last, without any chapter number repeating. For example, the first part (bab) includes the first and second chapters, followed by the second part which begins with the third chapter and ends with the eighth chapter, then the third part starts from the ninth chapter, and so on.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is the preface to the new edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The author begins by contrasting the approach of this book with traditional fiqh works and the Majalla. Traditional works proceed from specific rulings (furu‘) and scatter principles along the way, whereas his book gathers general principles from various chapters and derives them from the rulings and their causes, then presents them in a structured manner. He emphasizes that this task requires collaborative effort from jurists. The author then describes the distinguishing features of this new edition. In content, he has maintained the book's educational character as an introductory text for beginners, resisting turning it into an encyclopedia. He increased illustrative examples, added appendices at the end of some chapters for advanced students (not required for exams), kept shorter advanced footnotes marked with a star, and updated content to address contemporary issues such as bank interest, siyasa shar‘iyya, codification, and the hadith vs. ra’y debate. He also improved the index. In form, he reorganized chapters to have a continuous numbering across all parts, avoiding repetition. This preface sets the methodological tone for the entire book, emphasizing its pedagogical purpose over comprehensive coverage.

Key Terms
المبادىء العامة (al-mabādi’ al-‘āmma): General principles of fiqh that serve as foundations from which detailed rulings are derived or to which they are referred.
الأصول الكلية (al-uṣūl al-kulliyya): Universal maxims that encompass many rulings and are used to derive or organize furu‘.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, how does 'al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm' differ from traditional fiqh works?
A) It directly deals with detailed rulings and scatters principles as needed.
B) It gathers general principles from various chapters and uses rulings as examples.
C) It is a collection of fatwas on contemporary issues.
D) It only covers the Hanafi school rulings.

Key Takeaway
Al-Madkhal's methodology is principle-first, teaching fundamentals through examples, contrasting with traditional branch-first works.

Features of the New Edition: Content and Form
Author describes content and form features of new edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key content and form improvements in the new edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm as described in the preface.

Core Idea
The new edition balances educational simplicity with appendices for advanced study and contemporary relevance.

The preface details several improvements in the new edition. The author maintains the book's role as an introductory text for students without religious background, resisting turning it into an encyclopedia. He increased illustrative examples, added appendices for advanced students (not required), marked advanced footnotes with stars, and updated content with contemporary issues like bank interest and codification. Form-wise, he reorganized chapters with continuous numbering to avoid repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify content improvements
The author increased illustrative examples, added appendices for advanced topics, kept advanced footnotes but marked them, and added contemporary issues.
All these serve the educational purpose without overburdening beginners.
2
Understand the appendices system
Appendices at chapter ends contain detailed material for advanced students; they are not exam material for undergraduates. Some were originally lengthy footnotes.
This allows the book to serve multiple levels.
3
Recognize contemporary updates
New chapter on the eighth fiqh period, appendices on bank interest, siyasa shar‘iyya, codification, unification of laws, zina punishment, and hadith vs. ra’y.
Shows fiqh as a living tradition, not museum piece.
4
Note form improvements
Chapters are now continuously numbered across all parts, avoiding repetition of numbers.
Simplifies referencing and navigation.

ثم قد استحدثت الآن في هذا الإخراج الجديد، في أواخر بعض الفصول، ملحقات صغت فيها القضايا والمسائل التفصيلية والمتعمقة التي
تتعدى حاجة المبتدىء، لكنها تنفع الطالب المتقدم والمراجع الذي يريد التوسع والأصل في هذه الملحقات أنها تتجاوز حاجة الطلاب في مرحلة الإجازة (البكالوريوس) فلا تطلب منهم دراسة وامتحاناً. وبعض هذه الملحقات كان في الأصل حواشي مطولة في ثنايا الفصول، أما ما بقي من حواشي متعمقة لكنها لقصرها لا تستحق أن تفرد في ملحق، فحافظت على بقائها في أماكنها مع تمييزها بنجم ( ) ليتعداها الطالب دون حرج ويعلم. أنها ليست مطلوبة منه في الامتحانات.
كما عنيت في هذا الإخراج الجديد بتقريب المدخل - قدر ما يسمح به طابعه التعليمي - من الواقع المعاصر وقضاياه. فالفقه الإسلامي ليس تراثاً نضعه في المتحف وننفض عنه الغبار لنعرضه على الزوار، بل هو فهم للشريعة الإلهية التي ارتضاها الله للناس ليهتدوا بها في حياتهم العملية ويهدوا إليها الإنسانية. ومما أضيف إلى المدخل لهذا الغرض الآن : فصل جديد عن مميزات الدور الفقهي (الثامن) الذي نعيشه اليوم، وكذلك ملاحق متعددة تناولت فيما تناولته : حكم الفوائد المصرفية وسلطة ولي الأمر، والسياسة الشرعية، وتقنين الفقه والتقنين منه، وتوحيد التشريع في البلاد العربية وعقوبة الزنى والفرق بين مدرستي أهل الحديث وأهل الرأي (وهذه قضية قديمة تثور حولها تساؤلات معاصرة). أما الفهرس الهجائي التفصيلي للموضوعات والأعلام فقد جدد تجديداً
كاملاً حيث تفاقم في الطبعات السابقة الخلل فيه.
-
ޑ
-
ب - أما في الشكل : فبحسب هذا التقسيم الجديد تتتابع الفصول في المدخل الفقهي العام كله بالتسلسل من الفصل الأول إلى الأخير، دون أن يتكرر رقم أي فصل: فالباب الأول مثلاً يشمل الفصلين الأول والثاني ويليه الباب الثاني الذي يبدأ بالفصل الثالث وينتهي بالفصل الثامن، ليبدأ بعده الباب الثالث من الفصل التاسع وهكذا.
Preface to the new edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm
·
And general principles in a special order, to the branches of detailed rulings that are based on those general principles or are excepted from them. Our jurisprudence - including the Majalla al-Ahkam al-Adliyya - proceeds in the opposite manner: it directly deals with branches, and scatters parts of general principles and universal maxims along the way as appropriate. Gathering the parts of these general principles from various chapters, deriving them mostly from branches of rulings and their causes (illal), then joining each part to its counterpart to extract from each group the legal principle (asl shar‘i) that governs them and to which the branches are referred—all of this requires effort and time that should be undertaken cooperatively by a group of jurists and legal scholars dedicating all their talents to it.
...
Indeed, this new edition of the book after all its previous editions is distinguished in form and content.
·
(A) Content-wise: I have adhered to the educational character and style of this book so that it remains a preparatory text for students of Shari‘a and law colleges coming from general secondary education who have no religious background, and I resisted all temptation to turn the book into an encyclopedia of fiqh rulings or fatwas or an advanced reference for the minutiae and details of fiqh. Thus the book remains, as I originally intended it to be, an introductory preparatory text that teaches the university student the basic fiqh concepts and the sound method of fiqh thinking, not the details and branches of fiqh rulings found in traditional fiqh books. The fiqh rulings it contains serve primarily its educational purpose by providing examples, citing evidence, concretizing abstract concepts, and fixing the main issues in the student's mind. I have increased the number of carefully chosen illustrative examples to suit the need of the beginner for clarification.
Moreover, in this new edition I have introduced appendices at the end of some chapters, in which I have formulated detailed and advanced issues and questions that exceed the beginner's need but benefit the advanced student and the researcher who seeks expansion. The principle regarding these appendices is that they go beyond the need of students at the bachelor's level, so they are not required for study or examination. Some of these appendices originally were lengthy footnotes within the chapters; as for the remaining advanced footnotes that are too short to be detached as appendices, I kept them in their places, marked with a star (*) so that the student can bypass them without hesitation and know that they are not required in exams.
In this new edition I also aimed to bring the introduction as close as possible—to the extent permitted by its educational character—to contemporary reality and its issues. Islamic jurisprudence is not a heritage to be placed in a museum and dusted off for visitors; it is an understanding of the divine Shari‘a that Allah has chosen for people to be guided by in their practical life and to guide humanity thereby. Among what I have added to this introduction for this purpose now: a new chapter on the characteristics of the eighth fiqh period in which we live today, as well as various appendices that address among other things: the ruling on bank interest and the authority of the guardian (wali al-amr), siyasa shar‘iyya, codification of fiqh and its codification, unification of legislation in Arab countries, the punishment for zina, and the difference between the schools of hadith and ra’y (an old issue around which contemporary questions arise). As for the detailed alphabetical index of topics and prominent figures, it has been completely renewed because the previous editions suffered from increasing defects.
-
(B) Form-wise: According to this new division, the chapters in the entire al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm are arranged consecutively from the first chapter to the last, without any chapter number repeating. For example, the first part (bab) includes the first and second chapters, followed by the second part which begins with the third chapter and ends with the eighth chapter, then the third part starts from the ninth chapter, and so on.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is the preface to the new edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The author begins by contrasting the approach of this book with traditional fiqh works and the Majalla. Traditional works proceed from specific rulings (furu‘) and scatter principles along the way, whereas his book gathers general principles from various chapters and derives them from the rulings and their causes, then presents them in a structured manner. He emphasizes that this task requires collaborative effort from jurists. The author then describes the distinguishing features of this new edition. In content, he has maintained the book's educational character as an introductory text for beginners, resisting turning it into an encyclopedia. He increased illustrative examples, added appendices at the end of some chapters for advanced students (not required for exams), kept shorter advanced footnotes marked with a star, and updated content to address contemporary issues such as bank interest, siyasa shar‘iyya, codification, and the hadith vs. ra’y debate. He also improved the index. In form, he reorganized chapters to have a continuous numbering across all parts, avoiding repetition. This preface sets the methodological tone for the entire book, emphasizing its pedagogical purpose over comprehensive coverage.

Key Terms
المبادىء العامة (al-mabādi’ al-‘āmma): General principles of fiqh that serve as foundations from which detailed rulings are derived or to which they are referred.
الأصول الكلية (al-uṣūl al-kulliyya): Universal maxims that encompass many rulings and are used to derive or organize furu‘.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) They replace the main text of the chapters.
D) They are only for the teacher's use.

Key Takeaway
The new edition balances accessibility for beginners with depth for advanced readers through appendices and star-marked footnotes, all while remaining true to its educational mission.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Methodology of Revising a Fiqh Text: Al-Zarqa's Preface
Author explains changes in the new edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the pedagogical and methodological principles employed by Mustafa al-Zarqa in updating a classical fiqh introduction for contemporary education, and apply them to evaluating modern fiqh literature.

Core Idea
Islamic jurisprudence is a living guide, not a museum piece—it must address modern realities without compromising core principles.

In this preface, Mustafa al-Zarqa outlines the changes in the new edition of his seminal work, al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm. He explains that appendices are for advanced students and researchers, not beginners, and that the book now includes a chapter on the contemporary jurisprudential era and appendices on pressing modern issues like bank interest and codification. This lesson explores how to balance tradition with relevance—a skill essential for every mufti.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish tiers of content
Identify which content is for beginners (main text), which for advanced students (appendices), and which for quick reference (starred footnotes). Note the pedagogical rationale: appendices exceed bachelor's needs.
Al-Zarqa marks in-depth but short footnotes with a star so students can skip them without discomfort.
2
Recognise the contemporary turn
Observe the new chapter on the eighth jurisprudential era and appendices on bank interest, codification, and the schools of hadith vs. opinion. Understand that these additions aim to make fiqh relevant without distorting its foundation.
Al-Zarqa insists fiqh is not a museum relic but a practical guide.
3
Analyse structural improvements for usability
Identify the new consecutive chapter numbering, page headers with part and chapter, and vowelization for difficult words. Understand how these facilitate navigation and reading for researchers.
Previous editions had flawed indexes and repeated chapter numbers.
4
Appreciate collaborative scholarship
Note the roles: Sheikh Majd for hadith verification, Dr. Muhammad Anas for overall support. Understand that producing a reliable fiqh text requires specialised teamwork.
Al-Zarqa acknowledges the contributions explicitly, setting an adab example.

مقدمة الإخراج الجديد للمدخل الفقهي العام
ومن مزايا هذه الطريقة في التقسيم، فضلاً عن وضوحها، سهولة الإحالة فيها . فيكفي رقم الفصل ليتميز دون إضافة إلى الباب والقسم الذي ورد فيهما . ففي هذا الإخراج الجديد قد حلت الفصول بأرقامها المتسلسلة من أول الكتاب إلى آخره محل الفقرات المتسلسلة في الطبعات السابقة، وأصبح لكل فصل فقراته الخاصة به وتستأنف من الرقم (۱) في الفصل الذي يليه .
وفي هذا الإخراج الجديد ،وضعنا في أعلى كل صفحة من الكتاب الباب والفصل اللذين تعود إليهما تلك الصفحة بحيث يهتدي القارىء والمراجع من نظرة واحدة فيعلم أين هو ويسهل عليه الانتقال إلى أي باب أو فصل يريد. وقمنا بضبط الشكل للأحرف الضرورية في كل كلمة تحتاج إلى ضبط
لتسهيل قراءتها بالصورة الصحيحة على الطلاب.
أما الأحاديث النبوية الشريفة الواردة في الكتاب فقد تم تخريجها. وقد أعاننا في هذه المهمة وقام بها الشاب الناهض الشيخ مجد مكي الحلبي الذي يتابع دراسة الدكتوراه في الحديث النبوي، كما أعاننا في تصحيح تجارب الطباعة، أجزل الله مثوبته .
وأخيراً أشيد بالجهد الكبير الذي بذله ابني الدكتور محمد أنس الذي أعانني برأيه وخبرته وفعله إعانة لم يكن في الإمكان أن يتحقق هذا الإخراج الجديد ،دونها، إضافة إلى ما ألقاه منه من عون في سائر أمور حياتي، ولا سيما بعد تقدم سني وتوهن عظمي، فأسأل الله أن يجزيه خير
ما يجزي به عباده الصالحين المصلحين. وآخر دعوانا أن الحمد لله رب العالمين.
مصطفى احمد الزرقا
الرياض ١٢ من شوال ١٤١٦هـ
(الموافق ١٩٩٦/٣/١م)
Preface to the New Edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm.
They exceed the need of the beginner, but they benefit the advanced student and the researcher who wants expansion. The principle regarding these appendices is that they exceed the needs of students at the bachelor's level, so they are not required for study and examination. Some of these appendices were originally lengthy footnotes within the chapters; as for the remaining in-depth footnotes that are too short to deserve being placed in an appendix, I kept them in their places while marking them with a star ( ) so that the student can skip them without discomfort and know that they are not required in exams.
In this new edition, I also aimed to bring the introduction – as much as its educational nature permits – closer to contemporary reality and its issues. Islamic jurisprudence is not an inheritance we put in a museum and dust off to show visitors; rather, it is an understanding of the divine Sharia that God has chosen for people to guide them in their practical lives and to guide humanity to it. Among what has been added to the introduction for this purpose now: a new chapter on the characteristics of the eighth jurisprudential era that we live in today, as well as various appendices that addressed, among other things: the ruling on bank interest, the authority of the guardian, legal policy, codification of jurisprudence and its (lack of) codification, unification of legislation in Arab countries, the punishment for adultery, and the difference between the two schools of hadith scholars and scholars of opinion (this is an old issue that raises contemporary questions). As for the detailed alphabetical index of topics and personalities, it has been completely renewed because in previous editions its defects had worsened.
-
B – As for the form: According to this new division, the chapters in the entire al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm follow sequentially from the first to the last, without any chapter number being repeated. For example, the first part includes the first and second chapters, followed by the second part which starts with the third chapter and ends with the eighth chapter, then the third part starts from the ninth chapter, and so on.

Preface to the New Edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm
Among the advantages of this method of division, besides its clarity, is the ease of referral in it. The chapter number suffices for it to be distinguished without adding the part and section in which it occurs. In this new edition, the chapters with their consecutive numbers from the beginning of the book to its end have replaced the consecutive paragraphs in previous editions, and each chapter has its own paragraphs that restart from number (1) in the following chapter.
In this new edition, we placed at the top of each page of the book the part and chapter to which that page belongs, so that the reader and researcher can know in one glance where he is, making it easy to move to any chapter or part he wants. We also applied vowelization for necessary letters in every word that needed vowelization to facilitate correct reading for students.
As for the noble prophetic hadiths that appear in the book, they have been sourced. We were aided in this task by the diligent young man Sheikh Majd Makki al-Halabi, who is pursuing a PhD in prophetic hadith, and he also assisted in correcting printing proofs. May God reward him abundantly.
Finally, I commend the great effort made by my son Dr. Muhammad Anas, who assisted me with his opinion, experience, and action in a way without which this new edition could not have been achieved, in addition to the help he has given me in all other aspects of my life, especially after my advanced age and weakening bones. I ask God to reward him with the best reward He gives to His righteous, reformist servants. Our final prayer is that praise be to God, Lord of the worlds.
Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa
Riyadh, 12 Shawwal 1416 AH
(March 1, 1996 AD)
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is the preface to the new edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The author explains the structural and content changes in this edition. He notes that appendices are for advanced students and researchers, not beginners. He adds a new chapter on the contemporary jurisprudential era and appendices on modern issues like bank interest, codification, and the schools of hadith vs. opinion. He describes the new chapter numbering system that runs consecutively throughout the book, with no repeated numbers. Each page header shows the part and chapter for easy navigation. Vowelization is added for difficult words. Hadiths are sourced. He acknowledges Sheikh Majd Makki al-Halabi for hadith verification and his son Dr. Muhammad Anas for extensive assistance.

Key Terms
المدخل الفقهي العام (al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm): The title of the author's work, a general introduction to Islamic jurisprudence (fiqh).
الإخراج الجديد (al-ikhraj al-jadid): The new edition of the book, with structural and content revisions.
ملحقات (mulhaqat): Appendices added to the new edition covering contemporary topics and detailed discussions.
السياسة الشرعية (al-siyasah al-shar'iyyah): Legal policy: the discretionary rulings of the ruler to achieve public interest within Sharia guidelines.

Methodological Refinements in al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm
Author explains formatting improvements and acknowledgments for the new edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key structural enhancements in al-Zarqa's new edition and explain how they serve the mufti's methodology.

Core Idea
Clear chapter numbering and page headers transform a legal reference into a precision tool for the mufti.

In this front matter passage, al-Zarqa describes the improvements made to his classic work for easier navigation and study. While this may seem like mere formatting, these changes reflect deep pedagogical and methodological concerns: how a mufti or student can efficiently locate rulings, and how clarity in presentation reduces errors. This lesson explores how such structural decisions are part of the mufti's craft (adab al-mufti).

Guided Path
1
Identify the structural improvements

Understand the purpose of each improvement

3
Connect to the mufti's methodology

Introduction to the New Edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm
Among the advantages of this method of division, besides its clarity, is the ease of reference. The chapter number alone is sufficient to distinguish it without adding the section and part in which it appears. In this new edition, chapters with their consecutive numbers from the beginning of the book to its end have replaced the consecutive paragraphs in previous editions. Each chapter has its own paragraphs, and they restart from number (1) in the following chapter.
In this new edition, we placed at the top of each page of the book the section and chapter to which that page belongs, so that the reader and reference seeker can be guided with a single glance, knowing where they are, and making it easy to move to any section or chapter they wish. We also applied diacritical marks to necessary letters in every word that requires adjustment, to facilitate correct reading for students.
As for the noble prophetic hadiths mentioned in the book, they have been sourced. We were assisted in this task by the rising young scholar Sheikh Majd Makki al-Halabi, who is pursuing a PhD in prophetic hadith. He also helped us in correcting printing proofs. May Allah increase his reward.
Finally, I acknowledge the great effort made by my son, Dr. Muhammad Anas, who assisted me with his opinion, expertise, and action, without which this new edition could not have been achieved, in addition to the help he provided in my other affairs, especially after my advanced age and weakened bones. I ask Allah to reward him with the best of what He rewards His righteous, reforming servants. Our final call is that all praise is due to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa
Riyadh, 12 Shawwal 1416 AH
(3/1/1996 CE)
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the new edition of his influential work, al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm. It serves as front matter, explaining the methodological improvements made to enhance usability. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, highlights three key features: (1) a new numbering system where chapters are numbered consecutively from start to finish, replacing the old paragraph system; (2) headers at the top of each page showing the section (bab) and chapter (fasl) for easy navigation; and (3) the addition of diacritical marks (tashkil) on necessary letters to help students read correctly. He also notes that hadiths have been sourced (takhrīj), a task undertaken by Sheikh Majd Makki al-Halabi, and acknowledges the support of his son, Dr. Muhammad Anas. This introduction sets the stage for the reader to benefit from the book's structured presentation.

Key Terms
الإحالة (al-iḥāla): Reference or cross-reference within a book.
تخريج الحديث (takhrīj al-ḥadīth): Sourcing a hadith to its original collection and evaluating its chain.
ضبط الشكل (ḍabṭ al-shakl): Adding diacritical marks (tashkīl) to ensure correct pronunciation and reading.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Majallah: A Hanafi Codification as Foundation
Author's preface referencing the Majallah as a governing legal text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the historical role of Majallat al-Ahkam al-Shar'iyya and identify its significance as a Hanafi-based reference for modern legal reform.

Core Idea
The Majallah codified Hanafi fiqh into a civil code, serving as the general reference for Syrian law until new codes.

This lesson unpacks the opening of al-Zarqa's preface, where he sets the stage for his work under the authority of the Majallah. You will understand how a classical fiqh compilation became the backbone of a modern legal system, and why a mufti or legislator today still refers to it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal framework
Locate the phrase 'Majallat al-Ahkam al-Shar'iyya' and note its description: 'the general civil code and our reference in everything for which there is no legal ruling contrary to it.' This shows its default authority.
The Majallah was the Ottoman civil code, based entirely on Hanafi fiqh, consisting of 1851 articles covering transactions, torts, and procedure.
2
Understand the authority hierarchy
Note that the Majallah is described as the reference when no other statutory law exists. This establishes a supplementary role—primary but subject to later legislation.
In Hanafi fatwa practice, the Majallah is considered a reliable source for muftis in post-Ottoman states.
3
Connect to contemporary ifta
Reflect on how a mufti in Syria or elsewhere might use the Majallah today. Its Hanafi rules remain persuasive authority for transactions not covered by modern statutes.
For example, the Majallah's rules on gharar and riba are often cited in Islamic finance fatwas.

Introduction to the Third Edition
On the occasion of the issuance of the Syrian Civil Code during it
We began this edition of this General Jurisprudential Introduction under the authority of the Majallat al-Ahkam al-Shar'iyya, formulated from the fiqh of the Hanafi school, which was our general civil code and our reference in everything for which there is no legal ruling contrary to it.
Derived from it
It
And we intended for this jurisprudential series that we are formulating - Islamic jurisprudence in its new garb - to be a prelude to a modern civil code that we would produce in Syria from Islamic jurisprudence in its various rich schools, such that its foundations are based on the best of each of the eternal jurisprudential theories and principles, which were cultivated and refined by the genius jurists of Islam over thirteen centuries, and they created in its subjects and chapters - in addition to the rulings whose rules and structures they perfected - a language and terminology not known in the history of legal systems in terms of breadth, precision, and good selection.
Our hope is to create a civil code that links our legal legislation and our modern needs with a glorious jurisprudential past, capable - with its great principles and the flexibility of its rules and structures - of responding to all the needs of a righteous civil society and its economic, social, and customary developments, as we will see evidence of in this introduction.
And as guidance for this path, we wrote in this introduction a guiding study titled "Our Awaited Civil Code, and the Merit of Building It from Islamic Jurisprudence."

Commentary
This passage is the preface to the third edition of the book 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam' by Dr. Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The author explains the context of this edition: it coincides with the issuance of the Syrian Civil Code. He notes that this work was written under the shadow of the Majallat al-Ahkam al-Shar'iyya (the Ottoman civil code based on Hanafi fiqh), which served as the general civil code and reference for matters not covered by later statutes. The author expresses his aspiration that his series on Islamic jurisprudence in a new garb would pave the way for a modern civil code for Syria, drawing on the rich heritage of various Islamic schools of law, taking the best theories and principles from each. He praises the jurists of Islam over thirteen centuries for creating a precise legal language and robust rules. His hope is to produce a civil code that connects modern legal needs with the glorious jurisprudential past, capable of adapting to societal needs. He mentions that he included a guiding study titled 'Our Awaited Civil Code, and the Merit of Building It from Islamic Jurisprudence' in this introduction.

Key Terms
مجلة الأحكام الشرعية (Majallat al-Ahkam al-Shar'iyya): The Ottoman civil code formulated from Hanafi fiqh, serving as general civil code and reference.
قانون مدني (Qanun Madani): Civil code; a comprehensive set of laws governing private transactions.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

A Modern Civil Code from Islamic Jurisprudence: Al-Zarqa's Vision
Author's proposal for a new civil code based on Islamic jurisprudence from all schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the methodological approach of takhayyur (selecting the best from multiple madhahib) for modern legislation, as advocated by al-Zarqa.

Core Idea
Al-Zarqa envisioned a civil code selecting the best from all Islamic schools, showing Islamic law's adaptability and richness.

In this lesson, you will explore al-Zarqa's ambitious project: to create a Syrian civil code that draws from the entire Islamic legal heritage, not just one madhhab. You will learn how this approach, rooted in the flexibility of Islamic jurisprudence, can meet modern needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source materials
Al-Zarqa mentions 'Islamic jurisprudence in its various rich schools' as the pool for the new code. Note 'the best of each' indicates an eclectic method (takhayyur).
Takhayyur is a recognized method in Hanafi ifta, especially for muftis in contemporary settings.
2
Analyze the principles of selection
The author calls the theories and principles 'eternal' (khalidah) and 'cultivated by genius jurists over thirteen centuries.' This implies the code will be based on established fiqh, not invented rules.
Hanafi usul allows choosing stronger positions from within the madhhab or even across madhahib when codifying.
3
Connect to modern ifta practice
A mufti today can use takhayyur to issue fatwas that suit circumstances, e.g., choosing the Maliki view on a contract if it better serves public interest.
However, Hanafi muftis generally follow their own madhhab unless necessity dictates otherwise.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Syrian Civil Code and the Vision of Islamic Jurisprudence
Author describes the background and critique of the Syrian Civil Code

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the historical context of the Syrian Civil Code and evaluate al-Zarqa's critique of its adoption as a foreign code.

Core Idea
A foreign code cannot replace the deep-rooted flexibility of Islamic jurisprudence—true reform must emerge from within the tradition.

This preface to the third edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm sets the stage for the book's approach. Mustafa al-Zarqa recounts his original ambition to create a Syrian civil code from the rich heritage of Islamic fiqh, but laments the sudden adoption of the Egyptian (European-influenced) code after the 1949 coup. His critique reveals key principles about legal authenticity and the adaptability of Islamic law. In this lesson, we unpack the historical event and the author's vision, connecting it to the Hanafi tradition and modern codification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author’s original goal
Read the first section: Al-Zarqa intended to produce a civil code derived from Islamic jurisprudence (Hanafi and others) to replace the Ottoman Majalla. He believed this would connect modern needs with a glorious jurisprudential past.
The Majalla was based on Hanafi fiqh and served as the civil code before 1949.
2
Understand the historical event
The Syrian Civil Code was issued in 1949 after a military coup. It was essentially a copy of the new Egyptian Civil Code, which was heavily influenced by French law. Al-Zarqa describes this as a hasty and foreign imposition.
The coup leader was convinced by As'ad al-Kourani that adopting a foreign code would bring prestige.
3
Analyze the critique
Al-Zarqa’s main criticism: adopting a foreign code severs the legal system from its authentic roots and forces courts and lawyers to rely on foreign sources. He argues that Islamic jurisprudence has shown flexibility over centuries and can meet modern needs.
He calls the Majalla 'the greatest jurisprudential edifice in the world' – a strong stance from a Hanafi perspective.
4
Extract the author’s alternative vision
Instead of copying a foreign code, al-Zarqa proposes building a new code from the essence of Islamic fiqh, using its principles and methods to develop solutions for contemporary issues. This echoes the Hanafi tradition of legal reasoning (ijtihad) and adaptation.
He mentions 'derivations and renewals' (takhrijat wa tajdidat) as a continuous practice.
5
Connect to the Hanafi madhhab
The Hanafi school is known for its methodological flexibility (e.g., istihsan, 'urf). Al-Zarqa’s vision aligns with the idea that fiqh can evolve without abandoning its core principles.
The Majalla itself codified Hanafi fiqh; al-Zarqa wants to go further by drawing from all schools.

فأمنيتنا أن ننشيء قانوناً مدنياً يصل تشريعنا الحقوقي وحاجاتنا الحديثة فيه بماض فقهي مجيد، اخر قابل - بعظيم مبادئه ومرونة قواعده ومبانيه - أن يستجيب لكل ما تستدعيه حاجات المجتمع المدني الصالح وتطوراته الاقتصادية والاجتماعية والعرفية، كما سنرى شواهده في هذا المدخل.
وتوجيهاً إلى هذا الطريق كتبنا في هذا المدخل بحثاً توجيهياً بعنوان قانوننا المدني المنتظر، وفضل بنائه من الفقه الإسلامي".

غير أننا ونحن في هذا الطريق، وأبصارنا معلقة بنهايته، ووزارة العدل السورية تكلّف الإخصائيين بوضع قانون مدني مستمد من الفقه الإسلامي، وافٍ بالحاجات الزمنية الجديدة، فوجئنا بإصدار القانون المدني السوري في عهد الانقلاب العسكري الأول الذي حدث لدينا في ٣٠ آذار ١٩٤٩ . م ، وكان صدور هذا القانون بمساعي السيد أسعد الكوراني الذي ولأه زعيم الانقلاب وزارة العدل السورية. فقد اهتبل السيد الكوراني فرصة ذلك العهد الانقلابي والحكم الإرهابي، وأقنع زعيم الانقلاب الذي تولى السلطتين التشريعية والتنفيذية بأنّ إقامة قانون مدني أجنبي بدلاً من التشريع الإسلامي وفقهه في هذه البلاد هو خير وسيلة لخلود الذكر وعظيم المكانة في نظر الأجانب، وأوهمه أنَّ هذا العمل يجعله كنابليون الذي كان القانون المدني الفرنسي أكثر تخليداً له من فتوحاته !!
وقد وجدوا أنَّ القانون المدني المصري الجديد يحقق هذا الغرض لأنه أجنبي أوروبي المصادر، فأصدروه بين عَشِيَّة وضُحاها بِجَرَّة قلم، هدموا بها أعظم صرح فقهي في العالم، وأقاموا بها قانوناً لا مرجع فيه لقاض أو محام أو دارس إلا أصوله وإصطلاحاته الأجنبية.
وقد فاتهم أن طريق الخلود ليس في أخذ قانون أجنبي لا أثر لنا فيه إلا الانسلاخ من أصالتنا التي في كل أرض منها أثر ، وفي كل حضارة عنها خبر ؛ ولا نتيجة له إلا تناسي الذات والتحول إلى حياة على هامش الحياة وإنما طريق الخلود في أن ننشيء من جوهر فقهنا الذي ملأت آلاف مؤلفاته مكتبات العالم وأن نستمد من نبعه العَذب المعين الهدار قانوناً جديداً يفي بحاجاتنا الحديثة، فيكون أصله راسخاً في فقهنا، وفرعه شامخاً السماء، كما كان يفعل فقهاؤنا الأعاظم في تخريجاتهم وتجديداتهم الفقهية إزاء حاجات كل عصر ومصر، حتى بلغوا بالفقه الإسلامي هذه السَّعَة التي جلت عن الحدود. نعم هذا هو طريق الخلود الذي إذا مشينا وأنتجنا فيه كان كفيلاً بأن يرد مصر نفسها إلى الجادة بعدما خطئت وانساقت
Preface to the Third Edition
On the occasion of the issuance of the Syrian Civil Code during it
We began this edition of this general jurisprudential introduction under the authority of the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya, formulated from the fiqh of the Hanafi school, which was our general civil code and our reference in everything for which there was no legal ruling contradicting it.
Derived from it
And we had intended that this jurisprudential series that we are formulating, which is Islamic jurisprudence in its new garb, be a prelude to a modern civil code that we would produce in Syria from Islamic jurisprudence in its various rich schools, such that its foundations are based on the best of what each contains of eternal jurisprudential theories and principles, which have been cultivated and refined by the geniuses of Islamic jurists over thirteen centuries, and they created in its subjects and chapters - alongside the rulings for which they perfected their rules and structures - a language and terminology such that no jurisprudential language of such breadth, precision, and good selection has been known in the history of laws.
So our hope was to create a civil code that connects our legal legislation and our modern needs with a glorious jurisprudential past, capable - with its great principles and the flexibility of its rules and structures - of responding to all that the needs of a righteous civil society and its economic, social, and customary developments require, as we will see evidence of in this introduction.
And as guidance to this path, we wrote in this introduction a guiding research entitled 'Our Anticipated Civil Code, and the Virtue of Building it from Islamic Jurisprudence'.

However, while we were on this path, with our eyes fixed on its end, and the Syrian Ministry of Justice was charging specialists with drafting a civil code derived from Islamic jurisprudence, sufficient for new temporal needs, we were surprised by the issuance of the Syrian Civil Code during the era of the first military coup that occurred in our country on March 30, 1949. The issuance of this code was through the efforts of Mr. As'ad al-Kourani, whom the coup leader appointed to the Syrian Ministry of Justice. Mr. al-Kourani seized the opportunity of that coup era and terrorist rule, and convinced the coup leader, who held both legislative and executive powers, that establishing a foreign civil code instead of Islamic legislation and its jurisprudence in this country is the best means for immortal memory and great standing in the eyes of foreigners, and he deluded him that this work would make him like Napoleon, for whom the French Civil Code was more immortalizing than his conquests!!
They found that the new Egyptian Civil Code achieved this purpose because it is foreign and European in sources, so they issued it overnight with a stroke of a pen, by which they demolished the greatest jurisprudential edifice in the world, and established a code that has no reference for a judge, lawyer, or student except its foreign origins and terminology.
They missed that the path to immortality is not in adopting a foreign code in which we have no trace except the shedding of our authenticity, which has a trace in every land and a story in every civilization; nor does it result in anything except forgetting the self and transforming into a life on the margins of life. Rather, the path to immortality is that we create from the essence of our jurisprudence, whose thousands of works have filled the world's libraries, and that we draw from its sweet, overflowing, roaring spring a new code that fulfills our modern needs, so that its root is firmly planted in our fiqh and its branch reaches high to the sky, as our great jurists did in their jurisprudential derivations and renewals in response to the needs of every age and place, until they brought Islamic jurisprudence to this breadth that transcends limits. Yes, this is the path to immortality which, if we walk and produce in it, would be sufficient to return Egypt itself to the right path after it erred and drifted.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is the preface to the third edition of the book 'al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm' by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The author reflects on the historical context of the Syrian Civil Code. He begins by noting that the previous edition was written under the authority of the Ottoman Majalla (al-Majalla al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya), which was based on Hanafi fiqh and served as the general civil code and reference for any matter not covered by later legislation. His original ambition was to produce a modern civil code for Syria derived from the rich heritage of Islamic jurisprudence across all schools, selecting the best theories and principles. He emphasizes the flexibility and depth of Islamic legal language developed over thirteen centuries. However, while the Ministry of Justice was preparing a code derived from Islamic fiqh, a military coup in 1949 led to the sudden adoption of the Egyptian Civil Code, which was heavily influenced by European law. Al-Zarqa strongly criticizes this move, characterizing it as a hasty abandonment of the Islamic legal heritage. He argues that true progress lies in developing from within the Islamic tradition, not in copying foreign laws. The passage serves as a historical and methodological introduction, explaining the motivation behind the book and the author's perspective on legal reform.

Key Terms
المدخل الفقهي العام (al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm): The title of the book; a general introduction to Islamic jurisprudence, specifically Hanafi fiqh, by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa.
مجلة الأحكام الشرعية (Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya): The Ottoman Civil Code (al-Majalla) based on Hanafi fiqh, which served as the reference civil code before the Syrian Civil Code.
المرونة (al-muruna): Flexibility; the quality of Islamic legal rules and principles that allows adaptation to new circumstances, emphasized by al-Zarqa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Zarqa, what was the main problem with the Syrian Civil Code of 1949?
A) It was poorly written and full of errors.
B) It was derived from Islamic fiqh but incorrectly applied.
C) It was a foreign code that replaced the Islamic legal heritage.
D) It was opposed by the Syrian people.

Key Takeaway
Al-Zarqa's preface argues that Islamic jurisprudence, with its rich principles and flexibility, can and should form the basis of a modern civil code, rather than adopting foreign laws.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Al-Zarqa's Critique of Foreign Legal Imposition
Author recounts Syrian Civil Code enactment and defends Islamic jurisprudence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Zarqa's critique of adopting foreign civil codes and identify the proper methodology (takhrij) for integrating modern legal institutions into Islamic jurisprudence.

Core Idea
Legal reform must derive from Islamic jurisprudence, not copy foreign codes.

In the preface to the third edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm, Mustafa al-Zarqa recounts the shock of the Syrian Civil Code being enacted suddenly after a military coup, replacing Islamic jurisprudence with a European-inspired code. He argues that this was a catastrophic loss of a rich juristic heritage. However, he does not reject all borrowing; rather, he distinguishes between copying foreign law wholesale and adopting modern methods and new rulings grounded in Islamic principles through takhrij. This lesson unpacks his key arguments and the methodological path he proposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical context
Read the opening lines: al-Zarqa was working on a civil code from Islamic jurisprudence when the Syrian Civil Code was suddenly enacted after the 1949 coup. Understand the political pressure and foreign influence.
The coup leader was convinced by As‘ad al-Kurani that a foreign code would bring prestige like Napoleon's code.
2
Distinguish between borrowing methods and adopting substance
Al-Zarqa explicitly says he does not oppose borrowing (اقتباس) but emphasizes that Muslims are wealthy in substance (أثرياء في المادة). He advocates borrowing modern research methods (أساليب البحث الفقهي وترتيبه) and some new rulings (شركات المساهمة وعقود التأمين) – but only if derived on the principles of fiqh (تخريجاً يقيمها على أصوله).
The key is integration through takhrij, not wholesale replacement.
3
Understand takhrij as the mechanism for renewal
Takhrij al-fiqhi is the process of deriving new rulings from established principles to address novel situations. Al-Zarqa points to classical jurists (فقهاؤنا الأعاظم) who did this for every age and place, achieving the vast breadth of Islamic jurisprudence.
This is the Hanafi method of ijtihad within the madhhab.
4
Recognize the author's purpose for writing
Al-Zarqa expands his book to serve as a 'proof of Arab Islamic jurisprudence' (حجة الفقه العربي الإسلامي) and an awakening for the new generation, so they can judge the crime of abandoning their heritage.
The book is a defensive and revivalist project.
