وقد وجدوا أنَّ القانون المدني المصري الجديد يحقق هذا الغرض لأنه أجنبي أوروبي المصادر، فأصدروه بين عَشِيَّة وضُحاها بِجَرَّة قلم، هدموا بها أعظم صرح فقهي في العالم، وأقاموا بها قانوناً لا مرجع فيه لقاض أو محام أو دارس إلا أصوله وإصطلاحاته الأجنبية. وقد فاتهم أن طريق الخلود ليس في أخذ قانون أجنبي لا أثر لنا فيه إلا الانسلاخ من أصالتنا التي في كل أرض منها أثر ، وفي كل حضارة عنها خبر ؛ ولا نتيجة له إلا تناسي الذات والتحول إلى حياة على هامش الحياة وإنما طريق الخلود في أن ننشيء من جوهر فقهنا الذي ملأت آلاف مؤلفاته مكتبات العالم وأن نستمد من نبعه العَذب المعين الهدار قانوناً جديداً يفي بحاجاتنا الحديثة، فيكون أصله راسخاً في فقهنا، وفرعه شامخاً السماء، كما كان يفعل فقهاؤنا الأعاظم في تخريجاتهم وتجديداتهم الفقهية إزاء حاجات كل عصر ومصر، حتى بلغوا بالفقه الإسلامي هذه السَّعَة التي جلت عن الحدود. نعم هذا هو طريق الخلود الذي إذا مشينا وأنتجنا فيه كان كفيلاً بأن يرد مصر نفسها إلى الجادة بعدما خطئت وانساقت وراء التشريع الأجنبي، تفني نفسها فيه، وتبقى على هوامشه ضائعة الجهود، مُضَيِّعةً لمجد الجدود!! ونحن لا نأبى الاقتباس، فإنَّ الحكمة ضالة المؤمن، ولكننا أثرياء في المادة؛ وإنما نحن بحاجة إلى اقتباس الأساليب الحديثة في البحث الفقهي وترتيبه وإلى بعض الأحكام الجديدة التي نظمتها التشريعات للأوضاع الحقوقية والاقتصادية الحديثة كشركات المساهمة وعقود التأمين ؛ على أن نخرجها على قواعد فقهنا تخريجاً يقيمها على أصوله، ويدمجها فيه، كما كان يفعل فقهاؤنا الأعاظم تجاه الأوضاع والحوادث الجديدة التي كانوا يواجهونها . أما إهمال ذلك الفقه الذي تعاقَبَتْ على خدمته عشرات الأجيال من عباقرة الفقهاء وجهابذتهم ممن انقطعوا إليه ووقفوا كل مواهبهم عليه، وإقامة قانون أجنبي كامل يربطنا بعجلة التشريع والفقه الأجنبيين، ويجعل تراثنا العظيم نَسْياً منسيّاً، فهو إعلان إفلاس وليس باقتباس، وهو عجز لا إبداع، فلا يليق هذا بأمة لها ثروة فقهية كثروتنا وماض تشريعي جليل كماضينا . هذا وقد رأينا أنَّ خير عمل لنا، بعد تلك الجناية التي جنتها على مجد العروبة الفقهي أيد شعوبية أثيمة، هو أن نتابع صياغة هذه السلسلة الفقهية الجديدة بتبسط وإحكام كي يعرف الجيل العربي الحقوقي الجديد ما أفاد وما أضاع فنفتح له طريق الرجوع بعد أن يملك من المعرفة ما يحكم به على تلك الجناية وجُنَاتِها . فلذا عَمَدْنا إلى توسيع هذا المدخل الفقهي العام في طبعته الثالثة هذه التي صدر القانون المدني خلالها، ليكون هو والأجزاء التي تليه حجة الفقه العربي الإسلامي لأنصاره على أعدائه وموقظاً في الجيل العربي الناشيء غيرة على تراث فقهي ليس لأمة مثله في تاريخ التشريع. وبهذه المناسبة نذكر أنه في مثل هذا اليوم من العام الفائت (الثاني من تموز ١٩٥١ م) عَقَدت شعبة الحقوق الشرقية من المجمع الدولي للحقوق
But while we were on this path, our eyes fixed on its end, and the Syrian Ministry of Justice was charging specialists with drafting a civil code from Islamic jurisprudence that would meet new temporal needs, we were surprised by the issuance of the Syrian Civil Code during the first military coup that occurred in our country on March 30, 1949 CE. This code was issued through the efforts of Mr. As‘ad al-Kurani, whom the coup leader appointed as Syrian Minister of Justice. Mr. al-Kurani seized the opportunity of that coup era and terrorist rule, and convinced the coup leader – who held both legislative and executive powers – that establishing a foreign civil code instead of Islamic legislation and its jurisprudence in this country was the best means for eternal remembrance and great status in the eyes of foreigners. He deluded him that this action would make him like Napoleon, whose French Civil Code immortalized him more than his conquests!! They found that the new Egyptian Civil Code achieved this purpose because it is foreign and European in sources, so they issued it overnight with a stroke of a pen, by which they destroyed the greatest edifice of jurisprudence in the world, and established by it a law with no reference for a judge, lawyer, or student except its foreign origins and terminology. They overlooked that the path to immortality is not in adopting a foreign law in which we have no trace except the shedding of our authenticity – which has a trace in every land and a report in every civilization – and which results only in forgetting the self and transforming into a life on the margins of life. Rather, the path to immortality is that we create from the essence of our jurisprudence – whose thousands of volumes fill the world's libraries – and that we draw from its sweet, flowing, roaring spring a new law that fulfills our modern needs, so that its root is firmly planted in our jurisprudence and its branch rises high to the sky, just as our great jurists did in their legal derivations and renewals in response to the needs of every age and place, until they reached with Islamic jurisprudence this breadth that exceeded all limits. Yes, this is the path to immortality which, if we walk and produce in it, would be sufficient to return Egypt itself to the right path after it erred and followed foreign legislation, annihilating itself in it, remaining on its margins, wasting efforts, squandering the glory of ancestors!! We do not reject borrowing, for wisdom is the lost property of the believer, but we are wealthy in substance; rather we need to borrow modern methods of legal research and arrangement, and some new rulings that legislations have organized for modern legal and economic situations such as joint-stock companies and insurance contracts – provided we derive them upon the principles of our jurisprudence, establishing them on its foundations and integrating them into it, as our great jurists did regarding the new situations and incidents they faced. As for neglecting that jurisprudence – which tens of generations of genius jurists and intellectuals served, devoting themselves and dedicating all their talents to it – and establishing a complete foreign law that ties us to the wheel of foreign legislation and jurisprudence and makes our great heritage forgotten, that is a declaration of bankruptcy, not borrowing; it is impotence, not creativity. This does not befit a nation with a juristic wealth like ours and a glorious legislative past like ours. After that crime which the fingers of an evil chauvinism committed against the juristic glory of Arabism, we have seen that the best work for us is to continue formulating this new juristic series in an expanded and precise manner, so that the new Arab legal generation knows what it gained and what it lost, thereby opening for it the path of return after it possesses the knowledge to judge that crime and its harms. Therefore, we have undertaken to expand this general juristic introduction in this third edition that was issued during the civil code, so that it and the subsequent parts become a proof of Arab Islamic jurisprudence for its supporters against its enemies, and an awakening in the rising Arab generation of zeal for a juristic heritage that no nation has the like in the history of legislation. On this occasion, we mention that on this day of last year (July 2, 1951 CE), the Eastern Law Section of the International Academy of Law held...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the preface to the third edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. In this text, the author narrates the historical context of the Syrian Civil Code's enactment in 1949, immediately after the first military coup. He severely criticizes the adoption of a foreign (Egyptian/French) code as a replacement for Islamic jurisprudence, calling it a crime against the Arab juristic heritage. Al-Zarqa clarifies that he does not oppose borrowing beneficial elements from foreign systems, such as modern research methods and certain new legal institutions like joint-stock companies and insurance contracts, provided they are rooted in the principles of Islamic fiqh through proper derivation (takhrij). His main argument is that the path to legal progress and authenticity lies in developing new laws from the rich substance of Islamic jurisprudence, not wholesale adoption of foreign codes. This preface sets the motivation for expanding his book: to serve as a defense and revival of Islamic jurisprudence for the new generation of Arab jurists. The tone is passionate and polemical, reflecting the author's deep concern for the marginalization of Islamic law in modern Arab legal systems.

Key Terms
التخريج الفقهي (al-takhrij al-fiqhi): The process of deriving new rulings or laws from established principles of Islamic jurisprudence to address novel situations.
اقتباس (iqtibās): Borrowing; here, specifically the borrowing of legal methods and rulings from other systems, provided they are integrated into Islamic jurisprudence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Mustafa al-Zarqa, what is the correct approach for Islamic legal reform?
A) Complete rejection of any foreign legal concepts.
B) Wholesale adoption of Western civil codes.
C) Deriving new laws from Islamic jurisprudence while borrowing modern methods and integrating new rulings into fiqh principles.
D) Following only the classical rulings without any adaptation.

Key Takeaway
Legal reform must be grounded in Islamic jurisprudence through takhrij; borrowing is acceptable only if integrated into the school's principles.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Proper Method of Legal Borrowing (Iqtibas) in Islamic Fiqh
Author's defense and call to revive Islamic fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Zarqa's critique of blind legal borrowing and explain the Hanafi-derived method of integrating modern issues into Islamic fiqh.

Core Idea
Islamic fiqh is a rich, adaptable heritage — borrowing foreign laws wholesale is bankruptcy, not progress.

In this preface, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa delivers a passionate defense of Islamic jurisprudence against the trend of adopting foreign legal systems wholesale. He distinguishes between legitimate borrowing of modern methods and the disastrous abandonment of one's own legal heritage. This lesson unpacks the key argument and its implications for contemporary iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's main critique
Read the opening lines and note the strong language against those who 'waste themselves behind foreign legislation.' The author is responding to a trend of replacing Islamic fiqh with European codes.
Pay attention to the metaphor 'declaration of bankruptcy'.
2
Distinguish between legitimate and illegitimate borrowing (iqtibas)
The author accepts borrowing wisdom (al-hikma) and modern research methods, but insists that new rulings (e.g., for joint-stock companies, insurance) must be derived from Islamic legal principles, not imported wholesale.
He invokes the classical practice of deriving rulings for new situations.
3
Examine the historical example of the Paris conference
Al-Zarqa recounts the 1951 'Islamic Jurisprudence Week' where scholars presented on topics like ownership and riba. A French lawyer expressed surprise at the flexibility of Islamic law, contradicting the stereotype of rigidity.
This shows the external recognition of fiqh's adaptability.
4
Understand the author's call to action
The preface aims to educate the new Arab legal generation about the value of their heritage and to inspire them to revive fiqh, not abandon it. The expanded edition is a tool for this revival.
The tone is both defensive and aspirational.

مقدمة الطبعة الثالثة
وراء التشريع الأجنبي، تفني نفسها فيه، وتبقى على هوامشه ضائعة الجهود، مُضَيِّعةً لمجد الجدود!!
ونحن لا نأبى الاقتباس، فإنَّ الحكمة ضالة المؤمن، ولكننا أثرياء في المادة؛ وإنما نحن بحاجة إلى اقتباس الأساليب الحديثة في البحث الفقهي وترتيبه وإلى بعض الأحكام الجديدة التي نظمتها التشريعات للأوضاع الحقوقية والاقتصادية الحديثة كشركات المساهمة وعقود التأمين ؛ على أن نخرجها على قواعد فقهنا تخريجاً يقيمها على ،أصوله، ويدمجها فيه، كما كان يفعل فقهاؤنا الأعاظم تجاه الأوضاع والحوادث الجديدة التي كانوا يواجهونها . أما إهمال ذلك الفقه الذي تعاقَبَتْ على خدمته عشرات الأجيال من عباقرة الفقهاء وجهابذتهم ممن انقطعوا إليه ووقفوا كل مواهبهم عليه، وإقامة قانون أجنبي كامل يربطنا بعجلة التشريع والفقه الأجنبيين، ويجعل تراثنا العظيم نَسْياً منسيّاً، فهو إعلان إفلاس وليس باقتباس، وهو عجز لا إبداع، فلا يليق هذا بأمة لها ثروة فقهية ،كثروتنا وماض تشريعي جليل كماضينا .
هذا وقد رأينا أنَّ خير عمل لنا، بعد تلك الجناية التي جنتها على مجد العروبة الفقهي أيد شعوبية أثيمة، هو أن نتابع صياغة هذه السلسلة الفقهية الجديدة بتبسط وإحكام كي يعرف الجيل العربي الحقوقي الجديد ما أفاد وما أضاع فنفتح له طريق الرجوع بعد أن يملك من المعرفة ما يحكم به على تلك الجناية وجُنَاتِها .
فلذا عَمَدْنا إلى توسيع هذا المدخل الفقهي العام في طبعته الثالثة هذه التي صدر القانون المدني خلالها، ليكون هو والأجزاء التي تليه حجة الفقه العربي الإسلامي لأنصاره على أعدائه وموقظاً في الجيل العربي الناشيء غيرة على تراث فقهي ليس لأمة مثله في تاريخ التشريع.
وبهذه المناسبة نذكر أنه في مثل هذا اليوم من العام الفائت (الثاني من تموز ١٩٥١ م) عَقَدت شعبة الحقوق الشرقية من المجمع الدولي للحقوق المقارنة مؤتمراً في كلية الحقوق من جامعة باريس للبحث في الفقه الإسلامي تحت اسم «أسبوع الفقه الإسلامي برئاسة المسيو (متو Milliot) أستاذ التشريع الإسلامي في كلية الحقوق بجامعة باريس، دعت إليه عدداً كبيراً. أساتذة كليات الحقوق العربية وغير العربية وكليات الأزهر، ومن المحامين الفرنسيين والعرب ،وغيرهما ومن المستشرقين. وقد اشترك فيه من مصر أربعة أعضاء اثنان من جامعة فؤاد وعميد كلية الحقوق في جامعة إبراهيم وأحد أعضاء هيئة كبار العلماء عن الأزهر واشتركنا فيه أنا والأستاذ الدكتور معروف الدواليبي عن كلية الحقوق السورية.

٢٤
Preface to the Third Edition
[They] waste themselves behind foreign legislation, dissipating efforts in its margins, squandering the glory of ancestors!!
We do not reject borrowing, for wisdom is the lost property of the believer, but we are rich in substance; we only need to borrow modern methods in jurisprudential research and arrangement, and some new rulings that legislations have organized for modern legal and economic situations, such as joint-stock companies and insurance contracts; provided we derive them from the rules of our fiqh in a way that establishes them on its principles and integrates them into it, just as our great jurists did with the new situations and events they faced. As for neglecting that fiqh which tens of generations of genius jurists and their luminaries served, devoting themselves to it and dedicating all their talents to it, and establishing a complete foreign law that ties us to the wheel of foreign legislation and jurisprudence, making our great heritage a forgotten thing, that is a declaration of bankruptcy, not borrowing, and it is incapacity, not creativity. Such is not befitting a nation with a jurisprudential wealth like ours and a glorious legislative past like ours.
We have seen that the best work for us, after that crime committed against the jurisprudential glory of Arabism by an evil Shu'ubiyya hand, is to continue formulating this new jurisprudential series with detail and precision, so that the new Arab legal generation may know what it gained and what it lost, thus opening for it the path of return after it possesses the knowledge to judge that crime and its consequences.
Therefore, we have undertaken to expand this general jurisprudential introduction in its third edition, which witnessed the issuance of the Civil Code, so that it and the following parts may be a proof for Arab Islamic fiqh for its supporters against its enemies, and an awakener in the emerging Arab generation of zeal for a jurisprudential heritage unequaled by any nation in the history of legislation.
On this occasion, we mention that on this day last year (July 2, 1951 AD), the Oriental Law Section of the International Academy of Comparative Law held a conference at the Faculty of Law of the University of Paris to research Islamic jurisprudence under the name 'Islamic Jurisprudence Week', chaired by Monsieur (Milliot), Professor of Islamic Legislation at the Faculty of Law of the University of Paris. It invited a large number of professors from Arab and non-Arab law faculties and Al-Azhar faculties, French and Arab lawyers and others, and Orientalists. Participating from Egypt were four members: two from Fuad University, the Dean of the Faculty of Law of Ibrahim University, and a member of the Supreme Council of Scholars from Al-Azhar. I and Professor Dr. Ma'ruf al-Dawalibi from the Syrian Faculty of Law participated.
;
6(1)
(1)
The members lectured on five jurisprudential topics designated by the office of the International Academy of Comparative Law a year before, from the categories of public and private law (civil, criminal, administrative, and economic) and from the history of legislation. Invitations were sent for lectures on them: (1) Proof of ownership, (2) Expropriation for public benefit, (3) Criminal responsibility, (4) The influence of jurisprudential schools on each other, (5) The theory of usury in Islam. All lectures were in French, and each topic was allocated a day. After each lecture, important discussions were opened with the lecturer and among the participants, varying in length according to need, and their summaries were recorded.
During some discussions, one member, a former head of the Bar in Paris, stood up and said:
'I do not know how to reconcile what we were told about the rigidity of Islamic jurisprudence and its unsuitability as a legislative foundation to meet the needs of modern evolving society, with what we now hear in the lectures and discussions proving the complete opposite with evidence from texts and principles.'
(1) The names of the two universities mentioned are now, in the era of the Egyptian revolution, Cairo University and Ain Shams University, and the name of Farouk University in Alexandria became Alexandria University.
24
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is the preface to the third edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The author begins by strongly criticizing the trend of blindly adopting foreign legal systems at the expense of the rich Islamic jurisprudential heritage. He clarifies that he is not against borrowing wisdom in general, but emphasizes that Islamic fiqh is inherently wealthy and only needs adaptation of modern research methods and some new rulings—such as those for joint-stock companies and insurance—which should be derived according to Islamic legal principles, as classical jurists did. He warns that completely replacing Islamic fiqh with foreign law is a declaration of bankruptcy, not genuine borrowing.

Al-Zarqa then explains that the purpose of this expanded third edition is to educate the new Arab legal generation about the value of what they have lost and to provide a path back to their own heritage. He recounts the holding of an 'Islamic Jurisprudence Week' conference in Paris in 1951, organized by the International Academy of Comparative Law, where scholars presented on five topics including ownership, expropriation, criminal responsibility, influence of madhhabs, and riba. Importantly, he quotes a former head of the Paris Bar who expressed astonishment at the contrast between the alleged rigidity of Islamic fiqh and the actual flexible, text-based principles demonstrated in the conference. This preface serves as a passionate defense of Islamic jurisprudence and a call to revive and develop it on its own foundations.

Key Terms
الاقتباس (al-iqtibās): Borrowing or adopting ideas from external sources, here specifically foreign legal systems.
الشعوبية (al-shu‘ūbiyya): A prejudiced anti-Arab movement that sought to undermine Arab and Islamic achievements, blamed for the neglect of Islamic fiqh.
التخريج (al-takhrīj): The process of deriving new rulings from established legal principles and sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the proper approach to modern legal issues like insurance contracts?
A) Adopt foreign laws entirely as they are more advanced.
B) Reject all modern concepts and stick to classical rulings.
C) Derive rulings from Islamic legal principles using modern methodologies.
D) Ignore modern issues and focus only on traditional fiqh.

Key Takeaway
Islamic fiqh is a living tradition that can address modern issues through principled derivation (takhrij), not by wholesale adoption of foreign law.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
The 1951 Paris Conference: Recognizing the Adaptability of Islamic Jurisprudence
Historical account of a 1951 conference on Islamic jurisprudence in Paris.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of the 1951 Paris conference for the recognition of Islamic jurisprudence as a dynamic legal system and identify the features that enable its adaptability to modern needs.

Core Idea
The 1951 Paris conference affirmed that Islamic jurisprudence is not rigid but rich and adaptable, capable of meeting modern needs.

This passage from Mustafa al-Zarqa's introduction recounts a landmark conference in 1951 where Western and Muslim scholars examined Islamic jurisprudence and concluded that it has indisputable legal value and that the diversity of its schools grants it remarkable adaptability. This event is crucial for understanding the modern relevance of the Hanafi school and the principles of Iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Contextualize the Conference
Identify the organizing body (International Academy of Comparative Law), the venue (University of Paris), and the goal (study of Islamic jurisprudence).
This was not a Muslim-organized event but a Western academic initiative.
2
List the Topics Covered
The five jurisprudential topics demonstrate the breadth of issues discussed: proof of ownership, expropriation, criminal responsibility, influence of schools, and the theory of Riba.
These cover both private and public law, showing the scope of Islamic jurisprudence.
3
Analyze the Surprise of the French Bar President
His comment reveals the common Western misconception that Islamic law is rigid, and how the conference presentations and discussions proved otherwise.
This is a key moment illustrating the shift in perception.
4
Examine the Conference Report
The unanimously adopted report affirms the indisputable legal-legislative value of Islamic jurisprudence and the wealth in its diverse schools, enabling adaptation to modern life.
The report also recommends continued meetings and a dictionary of Islamic jurisprudence.
5
Connect to Modern Iftaa Methodology
The recognition of flexibility supports the use of principles like istihsan (juristic preference) and maslaha (public interest) in contemporary fatwa issuance.
This is the practical takeaway for muftis today.

Les Congressistes,
Etant donné l'intérèt suscité par les problèmes évoqués au cours de la SEMAINE DE DROIT MUSULMAN, et par les discussions auxquelles ils ont donné lieu, dont il est résulté clairement que les principes du droit musulman ont une valeur indiscutable, et que la variété des écoles à l'intérieur de ce grand système juridique implique une richesse de notions juridiques et de technique remarquable qui permet à ce droit de répondre à tous les besoins d'adaplation exigés par la vie moderne.

Introduction to the third edition
At the conclusion of the congress, the participants unanimously issued this report, which we translate below:
(1)
'The participants.
Based on the realized benefit of the investigations presented during the 'Islamic Jurisprudence Week' and the discussions that took place around them, which clearly concluded: a) That the principles of Islamic jurisprudence have an indisputable legal-legislative value. b) That the diversity of jurisprudential schools within this great legal system contains a wealth of concepts and information, and of principles worthy of admiration, and by which Islamic jurisprudence can respond to all demands of modern life and reconcile its needs.
They declare their desire that the Islamic Jurisprudence Week continue its work year by year, and they charge the congress office with preparing a list of topics that the discussions have shown the necessity of making the basis for research in the next session.
They hope that a committee be formed to compile a dictionary of Islamic jurisprudence to facilitate reference to the works of this jurisprudence, which would be a jurisprudential encyclopedia presenting
(1) This is the original French text of the aforementioned report:
Les Congressistes,
Etant donné l'intérèt suscité par les problèmes évoqués au cours de la SEMAINE DE DROIT MUSULMAN, et par les discussions auxquelles ils ont donné lieu, dont il est résulté clairement que les principes du droit musulman ont une valeur indiscutable, et que la variété des écoles à l'intérieur de ce grand système juridique implique une richesse de notions juridiques et de technique remarquable qui permet à ce droit de répondre à tous les besoins d'adaplation exigés par la vie moderne.

Paris, 7 juillet 1951.

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to the third edition of his work, providing a historical account of the 'Islamic Jurisprudence Week' conference held in Paris in 1951. The conference, organized by the International Academy of Comparative Law, brought together scholars from various countries to discuss Islamic jurisprudence. The author describes the five topics covered: proof of ownership, expropriation for public benefit, criminal responsibility, influence of juristic schools on each other, and the theory of riba. A notable incident is recounted where a former bar president in Paris expressed surprise at the adaptability and richness of Islamic law, countering the common misconception of its rigidity. The conference concluded with a unanimous report affirming the legal value of Islamic jurisprudence and the richness of its schools, and recommending the continuation of such meetings and the compilation of a dictionary of Islamic law. This passage sets the context for the book, highlighting the relevance and dynamic nature of Islamic jurisprudence in modern times.

Key Terms
الفقه الإسلامي (al-fiqh al-Islami): Islamic jurisprudence; the body of Islamic law derived from the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and analogical reasoning.
أسبوع الفقه الإسلامي (usbu' al-fiqh al-Islami): Islamic Jurisprudence Week; a conference series initiated in 1951 in Paris.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the main outcome of the 1951 Paris conference as described in the passage?
A) A declaration that Islamic law is outdated and needs reform.
B) An affirmation of the legal value of Islamic jurisprudence and its adaptability.
C) A decision to abandon the study of Islamic jurisprudence in favor of Western law.
D) A criticism of the diverse schools of Islamic jurisprudence for causing conflict.

Key Takeaway
The 1951 Paris conference demonstrated that Islamic jurisprudence, with its diverse schools, possesses the flexibility to address modern legal challenges, reinforcing the Hanafi school's methodology of adaptation through istihsan and maslaha.

The Vision for a Modern Fiqh Encyclopedia: Insights from the 1951 Paris Conference
Conference report and author's commentary on codification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two key conclusions of the 1951 Paris conference and explain why the author (al-Zarqa) regards an encyclopedia as the next crucial step for Islamic jurisprudence.

Core Idea
The 1951 Paris conference declared that Islamic jurisprudence must be codified into a modern encyclopedia to unlock its potential.

In this preface, Mustafa al-Zarqa shares the translated report from the International Week of Islamic Jurisprudence held in Paris in 1951. The report highlights the intrinsic value of Islamic legal principles and the richness of school diversity. It calls for a committee to compile a comprehensive encyclopedia of fiqh using modern methods. Al-Zarqa endorses this vision and sees his own work as a preliminary step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conference
Locate the conference name and dates: 'أسبوع الفقه الإسلامي' (Week of Islamic Jurisprudence) held in Paris in 1951.
The conference is a landmark event for modern Islamic legal studies.
2
Extract the two key conclusions
From the report, find the two points enumerated with (a) and (b): the undeniable legislative value of Islamic fiqh principles, and the richness of diversity among schools.
These conclusions affirm that Islamic law is both valuable and adaptable.
3
Understand the call for an encyclopedia
The report recommends forming a committee to compile a 'موسوعة فقهية' (fiqh encyclopedia) to present Islamic legal information according to modern methods.
This would make Islamic law accessible to contemporary scholars and jurists.
4
Analyze the author's commentary
Al-Zarqa elaborates that this encyclopedia is the necessary next stage for codification, and he notes that it should be undertaken by a committee of jurists and legal scholars, possibly under the League of Arab States.
He also mentions that a Faculty of Sharia in Damascus has started working toward this goal.

وفي ختام المؤتمر وضع المؤتمرون بالإجماع هذا التقرير الذي نترجمه فيما يلي: إن المؤتمرين». بناء على الفائدة المتحققة من المباحث التي عرضت أثناء «أسبوع الفقه الإسلامي»، وما جرى حولها من المناقشات التي تخلص منها بوضوح : أ ـ أن مبادىء الفقه الإسلامي لها قيمة حقوقية تشريعية) لا يُمارى فيها . ب - وأن اختلاف المذاهب الفقهية في هذه المجموعة الحقوقية العظمى ينطوي على ثروة من المفاهيم والمعلومات، ومن الأصول مناط الإعجاب وبها يستطيع الفقه الإسلامي أن يستجيب الحقوقية، هي لجميع مطالب الحياة الحديثة والتوفيق بين حاجاتها. يعلنون رغبتهم في أن يظل أسبوع الفقه الإسلامي يتابع أعماله سنة فسنة، ويكلفون مكتب المؤتمر وضع قائمة للموضوعات التي أظهرت المناقشات ضرورة جعلها أساساً للبحث في الدورة القادمة . للفقه الإسلامي يسهل ويأمل المؤتمرون أن تؤلف لجنة لوضع معجم الرجوع إلى مؤلفات هذا الفقه فيكون موسوعة فقهية تعرض فيها المعلومات الحقوقية الإسلامية وفقاً للأساليب الحديثة . ولا يخفى أنّ هذا الأمل الأخير الذي أعرب عنه المؤتمر في تأليف موسوعة فقهية على طراز موسوعات الحقوق الأجنبية، كموسوعة دالوز وغيرها، هو المرحلة الجديدة التي يجب أن يجتازها تدوين الفقه الإسلامي لكي يظهر بها جوهره ويدنو بها ثمره. وهذا من أعظم ما يجب أن تفكر فيه جامعة الدول العربية ومن الممكن أن يُعهد به إلى لجنة تتألف من بضعة أشخاص من الفقهاء والقانونيين، يتفرغون له منع المساعدين خلال بضع سنين. وإن كلفته لا تعد شيئاً بالنسبة إلى عظيم فائدته وأثره . والآن نترك المجال لهذا المدخل الفقهي أن يتكلم بلسانه العلمي: الهادىء، وأسلوبه الجديد المبسط الموطأ، وموازناته الفقهية المتواضعة، فيترجم هو عن هذا الفقه العظيم لكل قارىء، وأسأل الله تعالى التوفيق إلى خير طريق فهو الكفيل بالهداية إلى سواء السبيل. دمشق في ١٠ من شوال ۱۳۷۱ هـ ٢ من تموز ١٩٥٢ م. مصطفى احمد الزرقا (۱) وقد قامت الجمعية الدولية للحقوق المقارنة بتلخيص وقائع أسبوع الفقه الإسلامي هذا وما دار فيه من بحوث ومناقشات مع التعليق عليه بما يظهر أهميته الكبرى في عالم القانون، ونشرت هذه الخلاصة في ثلاثين صفحة من مجلتها المجلة الدولية للحقوق المقارنة ; (Revue internationale de droit compare) في العدد الرابع من السنة الثالثة، أيلول - تشرين الأول/ ١٩٥١ ، كما نشر معهد الحقوق المقارنة بجامعة باريس نصوص المحاضرات التي ألقيت في هذا المؤتمر كاملة مع مناقشاتها في كتاب خاص أصدرته مكتبة مجموعة سيريه Sirey للبحوث القانونية سنة ١٩٥٣ بإشراف المسيو (ميو) رئيس المؤتمر . (۲) إن هذا الحلم قد أوشك أن يتحقق، فقد أنشئت أول عام ١٩٥٤م الدراسي في الجامعة السورية بعد الطبعة الثالثة من هذا المدخل كلية للشريعة الإسلامية. وقد تبنت هذه الكلية مشروع وضع موسوعة (دائرة معارف) للفقه الإسلامي بالصورة التي تمناها هذا المؤتمر، ورصدت في ميزانيتها لعام ١٩٥٦ مبلغاً للبدء بهذا المشروع وألفت له لجنة وباشرت اللجنة اتصالاتها بعلماء الأقطار لهذا الغرض.
At the conclusion of the conference, the participants unanimously adopted this report, which we translate below: 'The participants...' Based on the benefit realized from the discussions presented during the 'Week of Islamic Jurisprudence' and the debates surrounding them, from which it clearly emerged: (a) that the principles of Islamic jurisprudence have an undeniable legal-legislative value; (b) that the diversity of jurisprudential schools within this great legal system contains a wealth of concepts, information, and foundational principles worthy of admiration, and thereby Islamic jurisprudence can respond to all the needs of modern life and reconcile its demands. They declare their desire that the Week of Islamic Jurisprudence continue its work year after year, and they charge the conference bureau with preparing a list of topics that the discussions have shown to be necessary as a basis for research in the next session. They hope that a committee be formed to compile a dictionary of Islamic jurisprudence to facilitate reference to the works of this jurisprudence, thus constituting a jurisprudential encyclopedia in which Islamic legal information is presented according to modern methods.' It is obvious that this last hope expressed by the conference—the compilation of a jurisprudential encyclopedia on the model of foreign legal encyclopedias, such as the Dalloz Encyclopedia and others—is the new stage that the codification of Islamic jurisprudence must pass through in order to reveal its essence and bring its fruit closer. This is among the greatest matters that the League of Arab States should consider, and it is possible that it could be entrusted to a committee composed of a few jurists and legal scholars who would devote themselves to it with the help of assistants over the course of a few years. Its cost is nothing compared to its great benefit and impact. Now we leave the field for this jurisprudential introduction to speak in its calm scientific language, its new, simplified, well-grounded style, and its humble jurisprudential balances, so that it may translate this great jurisprudence for every reader. And I ask Allah Almighty for success to the best path, for He is the guarantor of guidance to the straight path. Damascus, 10 Shawwal 1371 AH / 2 July 1952 CE. Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. (1) The International Association of Comparative Law has summarized the proceedings of this Islamic Jurisprudence Week and the research and discussions that took place, with commentary showing its great importance in the legal world, and published this summary in thirty pages of its journal, the Revue Internationale de Droit Comparé, in the fourth issue of the third year, September-October 1951. The Institute of Comparative Law at the University of Paris also published the full texts of the lectures given at this conference with their discussions in a special book issued by the Sirey Library for Legal Research in 1953 under the supervision of President Maillot. (2) This dream has almost been realized: at the beginning of the academic year 1954 in the Syrian University, after the third edition of this introduction, a Faculty of Islamic Sharia was established. This faculty adopted the project of compiling an encyclopedia of Islamic jurisprudence in the form desired by this conference, allocated an amount in its 1956 budget to begin this project, formed a committee for it, and the committee began its communications with scholars from various regions for this purpose.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is the preface to the third edition of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam. It opens with a translated report from the International Week of Islamic Jurisprudence conference held in Paris in 1951. The report highlights two key conclusions: (1) the undeniable legislative value of Islamic legal principles, and (2) the richness inherent in the diversity of schools within Islamic law, which enables it to adapt to modern needs. The conference expressed a desire to continue such gatherings and recommended the creation of a specialized committee to produce an Islamic legal encyclopedia following modern academic methods. The author, Mustafa al-Zarqa, then comments that this encyclopedia project is the necessary next step to unlock the true potential of Islamic fiqh in the modern age. He notes that the League of Arab States should take up this initiative, and that it can be achieved by a dedicated committee of jurists over a few years. He presents his own book, al-Madkhal, as an introductory work that paves the way for this larger project. The preface ends with the author's prayer for success. In footnotes, al-Zarqa mentions that the conference proceedings have been published in journals and books, and that in 1954 the University of Damascus established a Faculty of Sharia which has begun working on such an encyclopedia—thus the dream is approaching reality.

Key Terms
أسبوع الفقه الإسلامي (Usbu' al-Fiqh al-Islami): A conference (Semaine de Droit Musulman) held in Paris in 1951 dedicated to the study of Islamic jurisprudence.
موسوعة فقهية (Mawsu'a Fiqhiyya): An Islamic legal encyclopedia compiling all fiqh knowledge according to modern academic methods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To establish a new Islamic university
B) To form a committee to compile an Islamic legal encyclopedia
C) To unify all Islamic schools of law into one
D) To translate all Islamic legal texts into French

Key Takeaway
The 1951 Paris conference called for a modern encyclopedia of Islamic jurisprudence, viewing school diversity as a resource for adaptation—a vision that began to materialize in Damascus shortly after.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Introduction to al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm: The Challenge of Modern Hanafi Codification
Author's preface introducing the work's methodology and historical context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's motivation for writing al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm and explain the relationship between the Majalla and the broader Hanafi corpus in the context of modern legal reform.

Core Idea
Mustafa al-Zarqa called for a comprehensive fiqh encyclopedia to present Hanafi law in a modern, systematic, and accessible form.

This passage from the preface and original sermon of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm reveals the author's vision: to bring Islamic fiqh, particularly the Hanafi school, into the modern academic fold. Al-Zarqa critiques the existing method of scattered article-based commentary and aspires to create a work that rivals Western legal encyclopedias while remaining faithful to the Hanafi tradition. Understanding this context helps you appreciate why al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm adopts a comparative and subject-based approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's central aspiration
Read the passage carefully: what does al-Zarqa describe as the new stage that Islamic fiqh codification must pass through? He mentions a fiqh encyclopedia modeled on foreign works like Dalloz.
This is the key thesis of the preface.
2
Analyze the structure of Hanafi civil law in Syria
The original book preface outlines three layers: the Majalla, supplementary scattered rulings from Hanafi books, and later laws that amended parts. Understand this hierarchy.
The Majalla is not the exclusive source; it's a selection.
3
Identify the methodological critique
Al-Zarqa criticizes the existing commentaries for being article-by-article explanations without thematic organization. He advocates for a subject-based approach like French civil law textbooks.
This explains why al-Madkhal is organized by subjects (chapters on contracts, property, etc.) rather than by legal codes.
4
Evaluate the author's 'fiqhi entrance' concept
The book is called 'al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm' meaning 'The General Fiqh Entrance'. Al-Zarqa positions it as a gateway to understanding Islamic fiqh with a balanced, comparative style.
It is not a comprehensive legal manual but an introductory work that prepares students.

And from Him we seek help. The Sermon of the Book
After this, the civil rulings in our country are not confined to a code like the civil laws of other nations. Rather, our civil law is as vast as the ocean: it is the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya selected from the fiqh of the Hanafi school, and beyond it are the scattered fiqh rulings in the books of that school that are not stipulated in the Majalla, and then the laws that have abrogated or amended many of those fiqh rulings.
(1)
These civil Sharia rulings found in our books of fiqh and the Majalla have not yet been presented in a subject-based research style like what we see in civil law works prepared for university study in foreign nations, such as the books of Josserand and Capitant in French civil law. Rather, the commentaries on the Majalla and other fiqh books were based on the method of explaining individual articles and listing scattered rulings.

(1) We draw the reader's attention to the fact that this book and its preface were written and printed before the abolition of the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya and its replacement by a new civil law of foreign origin in Syria in 1949 CE, as we explained in the preface to the third edition.

Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a front matter section from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. It contains two parts: the author's preface to the third edition (dated 1952) and the original sermon (khutba) of the book. In the preface, al-Zarqa expresses the hope that Islamic fiqh will be codified into a comprehensive encyclopedia modeled on Western legal encyclopedias like Dalloz. He considers this the necessary next stage for Islamic jurisprudence to reveal its essence and bear fruit. He suggests the League of Arab States should undertake this project, possibly by forming a committee of fuqaha' and jurists. He notes that this dream nearly came true when the Syrian University established a Faculty of Islamic Sharia in 1954 and began planning such an encyclopedia. The author then introduces his work as a 'fiqhi entrance' that will speak with a balanced scientific style and comparative approach. The original book preface (خطبة الكتاب) then describes the state of Hanafi civil law in Syria: its primary source is the Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya (a codification of Hanafi fiqh), supplemented by other scattered rulings in Hanafi books and later legislative amendments. Al-Zarqa criticizes the existing literature for lacking a systematic, subject-based methodology like French civil law textbooks. He notes that students graduating from secondary schools need a better-organized presentation. This passage sets the stage for his work's methodology: to present Islamic fiqh in a modern, comparative, and accessible manner while remaining firmly rooted in the Hanafi tradition. The authorial voice is clear: he is a reformer who values both classical fiqh and contemporary legal science.

Key Terms
مجلة الأحكام العدلية (Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya): The Ottoman civil code of the Hanafi school, a codification of selected Hanafi rulings used as the primary civil law in Syria before 1949.
المذهب الحنفي (al-madhhab al-hanafi): The Hanafi school of Islamic law, founded by Abu Hanifa, followed by the majority of Sunni Muslims in Syria and the Ottoman Empire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal represents a reformist effort to present Hanafi fiqh in a modern, systematic, and comparative style while preserving its substantive authority.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Need for Systematic Legal Education: Al-Zarqa's Critique and Method
Author's preface: critique of traditional fiqh textbooks and proposal for a new pedagogical method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the limitations of traditional fiqh books for university education and explain Al-Zarqa's proposed systematic research method as a solution.

Core Idea
Traditional fiqh books are reference tools for judges, not textbooks for students—systematic organization is key to legal learning.

In this preface to his seminal work on obligations and contracts, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa diagnoses a critical gap in Islamic legal education. He contrasts the traditional article-by-article commentaries with the systematic, subject-based method used in Western law schools, arguing that students need a clear conceptual framework, not scattered rulings to memorize.

Guided Path
1
Identify the current state of fiqh textbooks
Read Al-Zarqa's description of how fiqh books and Majallah commentaries are organized. He says they explain articles individually and list scattered rulings.
This is the 'article-by-article' method.
2
Understand the student's struggle
Al-Zarqa explains that a new law student lacks knowledge of fiqh principles, terminology, and theories, so he is forced to memorize sub-rulings without understanding their foundations.
Note his phrase: 'without foundations that hold these branches in his mind'.
3
Identify the proposed solution
Al-Zarqa advocates for a 'systematic research method' (al-bahth al-mawdu'i) that organizes rulings by subject and explains underlying rules and theories. This makes the material easier to understand and remember.
Contrast this with the existing 'shuruh al-majallah' method.
4
Note the author's personal commitment
Al-Zarqa states that since 1944, he resolved to follow this new method in his teaching and writing, leading to this book on obligations and contracts.
This shows his practical implementation of the reform.

وإياه نستعين خُطبة الكِتاب
وبعد، فإن الأحكام المدنية لدينا ليست محصورة في مجموعة على نحو القوانين المدنية في الأمم الأخرى، وإنما القانون المدني لدينا في سَعَة البحر المحيط فهو مجلة الأحكام العدلية المختارة من فقه المذهب الحنفي ، ومن ورائها سائر الأحكام الفقهية المنثورة في كتب ذلك المذهب مما لا نص عليه في المجلة، ثم القوانين التي تناولت كثيراً من تلك الأحكام الفقهية بالنسخ أو التعديل.
(1)
وهذه الأحكام الشرعية المدنية مما في كتب الفقه والمجلة لدينا لم تُعرض إلى اليوم بأسلوب البحث الموضوعي على نسق ما نشاهده في مؤلفات القانون المدني المهيأة للدراسة الجامعية في الأمم الأجنبية، ككتب «جوسران» و «كابيتان مثلاً في القانون المدني الفرنسي، بل كانت شروح المجلة والكتب الفقهية الأخرى قائمة على طريقة شرح المواد مفردة، وسرد الأحكام المتفرقة.
والطالب الذي يتخرَّج من مدارس التحصيل الثانوي العام. فيدخل

م كما بيناه في مقدمة الطبعة الثالثة.
٢٧
كلية الحقوق لا يستطيع فهم تلك الأحكام الفقهية وهضمها ما دام يواجه فيها منذ البداية فروع المسائل التي يتوقف فهمها على قواعد وعلل ونظريات ومبادىء ولغة واصطلاحات فقهية يجهلها الطالب جميعاً، فيضطر أن يحفظ تلك المسائل الفرعية وأحكامها حفظاً، دون أسس تمسك بهذه الفروع في فكره ورابطة موضوعية تجمع بعضها إلى بعض .
فالكتب الفقهية لدينا وشروح المجلة كلها في الحقيقة إنما تصلح أن تكون مدونات للمحاكم كجميع شروح القوانين، ليرجع إليها الحكام عند حاجاتهم إلى معرفة ما حول كل مادة وحكم من إيضاح وتفصيل، ولا تصلح أن تكون كتباً تعليمية في مجلة الأحكام العدلية الشرعية ومبادئها الفقهية لطلاب الحقوق في الجامعات.
ونحن بحاجة شديدة، إلى كتب جديدة توضع على طريقة البحث الموضوعي في أحكام المجلة ومبادئها الفقهية لتصبح بالتبسيط والتركيز والتنسيق قريبة المتناول، سهلة المأخذ على أفهام الطلاب وحفظهم، حتى يتحقق في تأليف هذا العلم الدقيق الهام تمييز حسن بين الحاجة التعليمية في الجامعات والحاجة التطبيقية في المحاكم ويعرض الفقه الإسلامي في ثوب قشيب وأسلوب جديد يساير ذوق العصر ولغته، ولتمكن عندئذ مقارنة مباحثه بنظائرها من المباحث والنظريات القانونية فيظهر بذلك ما في فقهنا الجليل من مكنونات ثمينة في ميزان التشريع. وإني منذ أن عُهِدَ إليَّ بتدريس الحقوق المدنية التي كان أساسها مجلة : الأحكام العدلية في كلية الحقوق السورية سنة (١٣٦٣ هـ = ١٩٤٤ م) وجهت هَمِّي وعَقَدْتُ عزمي على أَنْ أَنهج في عرض فقه المجلة تدريساً وتأليفاً هذا المنهج الضروري اليوم، وأن أتقرب من جادته ما استطعت ... فشرعت في وضع هذا الكتاب المتسلسل عن الالتزامات والعقود في الفقه الإسلامي لأفتح به جادة جديدة لتدريس الحقوق المدنية في البلاد السورية، جامعاً فيه الأحكام المدنية العامة المعمول بها لدينا مما تضمنته مجلة الأحكام الشرعية وما يتصل بها من المباحث والمسائل الفقهية
And from Him we seek help. Introduction of the Book. After [this], indeed the civil rulings in our [country] are not confined to a compilation like the civil codes of other nations; rather, our civil law is in the expanse of the encompassing sea: it is the Majallah al-Ahkam al-Adliyyah selected from the fiqh of the Hanafi school, and behind it are the rest of the fiqh rulings scattered in the books of that school which are not stipulated in the Majallah, then the laws that have abrogated or amended many of those fiqh rulings. (1) And these Shariah civil rulings found in the fiqh books and the Majallah have not until today been presented in a systematic research style like what we see in civil law works prepared for university study in foreign nations, such as the books of Josserand and Capitant, for example, in French civil law. Rather, the commentaries on the Majallah and other fiqh books were based on the method of explaining articles individually and listing scattered rulings. And the student who graduates from general secondary schools and enters the Faculty of Law cannot understand and digest those fiqh rulings as long as he encounters from the beginning branches of issues whose understanding depends on rules, causes, theories, principles, language, and juristic terminology that the student is entirely ignorant of; so he is forced to memorize those subsidiary issues and their rulings by rote, without foundations that hold these branches in his mind and a substantive connection that links them together. Indeed, our fiqh books and the commentaries on the Majallah are all in reality only suitable as law compilations for courts, like all legal commentaries, for judges to refer to when they need to know the clarification and detail surrounding each article and ruling, and they are not suitable as educational books on the Shariah civil Majallah and its fiqh principles for law students in universities. And we are in dire need of new books composed on the systematic research method regarding the rulings of the Majallah and its fiqh principles, so that through simplification, concentration, and coordination they become easily accessible, easy to grasp for students' understanding and memory, until a good distinction is achieved in the composition of this precise and important science between the educational need in universities and the applied need in courts, and Islamic jurisprudence is presented in a fresh garment and a new style that aligns with the taste of the age and its language, and then its investigations can be compared with their counterparts from legal investigations and theories, thereby showing what our great fiqh contains of precious treasures in the scale of legislation. And since I was entrusted with teaching civil law, which was based on the Majallah al-Ahkam al-Adliyyah at the Syrian Faculty of Law in 1363 AH = 1944 AD, I directed my effort and resolved to follow this methodology, which is essential today, in presenting the fiqh of the Majallah in teaching and authorship, and to approach its path as much as I could. So I began composing this sequential book on obligations and contracts in Islamic jurisprudence to open a new path for teaching civil law in the Syrian lands, collecting therein the general civil rulings operative in our [country] from what the Majallah al-Ahkam al-Shar'iyyah contained and what relates to it of juristic investigations and issues.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface (khutbat al-kitab) introducing his work. Al-Zarqa begins by describing the state of Islamic civil law in his time: it is not codified in a single code like Western civil codes, but rather consists of the Majallah (a selection of Hanafi fiqh) supplemented by other scattered rulings from Hanafi books, plus later laws that have modified or abrogated parts. He then critiques the existing fiqh textbooks and Majallah commentaries: they are arranged article by article, listing isolated rulings without systematic organization, making them suitable only as reference works for judges but not as textbooks for university students. A student entering law school lacks the necessary background in fiqh principles, terminology, and theory, so he merely memorizes sub-rulings without understanding their underlying foundations. Al-Zarqa calls for new books written in a 'systematic research' (al-bahth al-mawdu'i) style, simplified and organized, to meet both educational and practical needs. He states his personal resolve to adopt this method when he began teaching civil law at the Syrian Faculty of Law in 1944, leading to this book on obligations and contracts. The tone is scholarly and reformist, reflecting the modernizing trends in Syrian legal education at the time.

Key Terms
مجلة الأحكام العدلية (Majallah al-Ahkam al-Adliyyah): The Ottoman civil code (1876) based on Hanafi fiqh, a selection of rulings organized in articles.
البحث الموضوعي (al-bahth al-mawdu'i): Systematic, subject-based research method organizing legal topics thematically rather than by individual articles.
شروح المجلة (shuruh al-majallah): Commentaries on the Majallah, explaining each article and providing examples and subsidiary rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Zarqa, what is the main problem with traditional fiqh books and Majallah commentaries for university law students?
A) They are too expensive and hard to find.
B) They are arranged article by article without systematic organization, requiring students to memorize isolated rulings without grasping underlying principles.
C) They focus only on criminal law and ignore civil matters.
D) They are written in a foreign language that students cannot understand.

Key Takeaway
Al-Zarqa argues that Islamic legal education requires textbooks organized by subject with underlying principles, not just article-by-article commentaries suitable only for court references.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Al-Zarqa's Diagnosis and the Objective Method
Author's methodological preface: diagnosing educational deficiencies and proposing new approach

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Zarqa's critique of traditional fiqh education and explain the 'objective method' (al-manhaj al-mawḍūʿī) as a pedagogical approach for teaching Hanafi fiqh in universities.

Core Idea
Traditional fiqh books obscure the essence; the objective method builds rulings from general principles, not scattered branches.

In this preface from his monumental al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm, Shaykh Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa diagnoses a fundamental flaw in how Hanafi fiqh has been taught to law students. He argues that presenting branch issues (furu') without first establishing the underlying rules and principles forces students into rote memorization, preventing true understanding. He proposes a new 'objective method' that organizes fiqh around general theories, proceeding from simple to complex, thereby making Islamic jurisprudence accessible and comparable to modern legal systems.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
What does al-Zarqa identify as the core educational failure in existing fiqh books? Look for his description of students 'facing branches from the beginning' without knowing the rules and principles.
He says the books are 'suitable for courts but not for teaching'.
2
Distinguish the two needs
What is the difference between the educational need of universities and the practical need of courts? The author calls for a distinction between 'al-haja al-ta'limiyya' (educational need) and 'al-haja al-tatbiqiyya' (practical need).
3
Define the objective method
What are the key features of al-Zarqa's proposed teaching methodology? Look for terms like 'al-manhaj al-mawḍūʿī', 'simplification', 'concentration', 'coordination', and 'from simple to complex'.
It is the opposite of the 'furu'i' method.
4
Locate the Hanafi basis
Why does the author adopt the Hanafi school as the foundation? He states it is 'the school applied in the judiciary' (al-madhhab al-muʿamal bihi fi al-qaḍāʾ).
Other schools are referenced as needed.
5
State the ultimate goal
What does al-Zarqa hope to achieve by reframing Islamic fiqh into a general theory? He wants to 'reveal the precious essence' and allow comparison with modern legal theories.
He mentions the general theory of obligations (naẓariyyat al-iltizām).

وقد اتخذت فيه المذهب الحنفي في الفقه الإسلامي أساساً للبحث لأنه المعمول به في القضاء، مع الإلمام بالمذاهب الأخرى في بعض المواطن بحسب حاجة البحث .

(۱) ينظر التعريف بنظرية الإلتزام العامة الأجنبية في الجزء الثالث من هذه السلسلة. (۲) تسوغ النسبة إلى لفظ الجمع إذا صارت صيغته في الاستعمال كاسم العلم مثل (أنصاري) في النسبة إلى (الأنصار)، وكذا إذا كانت النسبة إلى المفرد تلبس المعنى المراد بغيره كما هنا، إذ لو قيل (فرعي) لما فهم منه معنى طريقة سرد الفروع، بل يفهم منه ما يقابل معنى (أصلي). ومثل ذلك في العرف القانوني اليوم كلمة (حقوقي) نسبة إلى الحقوق بمعنى العلم، فلو نسب إلى المفرد فقيل : (حقي) لالتبس المعنى المراد بغيره. وقد استعمل قدماء الفقهاء والأصوليين النسبة إلى (الفروع) بصيغة الجمع، فقالوا : فروعي إما باعتبار أن لفظ «الفرع صار كاسم علم المسائل الفقه، وإما لدفع الالتباس المذكور (انظر عبارة أبي إسحاق الشاطبي الآتية في الفقرة (۱/۱۹ ) على أنه يجوز في لغة أن ينسب إلى الجمع مطلقاً. (ر: حاشية الصبان على الأشموني في بحث ياء النسب).

Book Preface: The College of Law cannot understand and digest those fiqh rulings as long as they confront from the beginning the branches of issues whose understanding depends on rules, causes, theories, principles, and a fiqh language and terminology that the student is entirely ignorant of, so he is forced to memorize those subsidiary issues and their rulings by heart, without foundations that hold these branches in his mind and a subject-matter link that gathers them together. So the fiqh books we have and the commentaries on al-Majalla are all in reality only suitable to be records for courts like all commentaries on laws, for judges to refer to when they need to know explanations and details around each article and ruling, and they are not suitable to be educational books on the Islamic Judicial Code (Majallat al-Ahkam al-'Adliyya) and its fiqh principles for law students in universities. And we are in dire need of new books written on the objective research method regarding the rulings of al-Majalla and its fiqh principles, so that with simplification, focus, and organization they become within easy reach and easily understood by students' minds and memories, until a good distinction is achieved in the writing of this precise and important subject between the educational need in universities and the practical need in courts, and Islamic fiqh is presented in a beautiful garb and new style that goes along with the taste of the age and its language, and so its topics can be compared with their counterparts from legal investigations and theories, thereby revealing what is in our sublime fiqh of precious treasures in the balance of legislation. And since I was entrusted with teaching civil law, whose basis was al-Majalla, in the Syrian Law School in the year 1363 AH = 1944 CE, I directed my effort and resolved to follow this necessary approach in presenting the fiqh of al-Majalla in teaching and writing, and to draw near to its path as much as I could... So I began writing this serial book on obligations and contracts in Islamic fiqh to open a new path for teaching civil law in Syrian lands, gathering in it the general civil rulings in effect among us from the Majallat al-Ahkam al-Shar'iyya and what relates to it of important fiqh investigations and issues, with reference to legal amendments that occurred to the original fiqh rulings since the Ottoman era in these Syrian lands until today. And I have taken the Hanafi school in Islamic fiqh as the basis for research because it is the one applied in the judiciary, while being acquainted with other schools in some places according to the need of research. And my goal in it is to transform the formulation of Islamic fiqh, so I build from its rules and principles a general theory along the lines of the general theory of obligations in modern foreign legal fiqh, serving our sublime Islamic fiqh so that its precious essence becomes apparent, which was veiled by the old style that has become difficult for contemporary people to digest; and fulfilling the need for the wise educational method in university study of this precise subject, with its scattered issues, numerous investigations, wide horizons, and great importance and status. That is because civil law, which is called 'civil code', is the foundation of all legal studies and understandings, and the educational need in it requires an objective method that proceeds from the simple to the complex, and the old furu'i method, in which branches are not built on their principles in a comprehensive general theory, is no longer digestible. (1) See the definition of the foreign general theory of obligations in the third part of this series. (2) Attribution to the plural form is permissible if its usage becomes like a noun, such as 'Ansari' in attribution to 'al-Ansar', and likewise if attributing to the singular would obscure the intended meaning, as here, because if it were said 'far'i' it would not be understood to mean the method of enumerating branches, but rather would be understood as the opposite of 'asli'. Similarly in today's legal custom, the word 'huquqi' in attribution to 'al-huquq' (law) meaning the science, so if attributed to the singular and said 'haqqi', the intended meaning would be confused. The early jurists and usuliyyun used attribution to 'furu' in the plural form, saying 'furu'i', either considering the word 'far' as a proper noun for fiqh issues, or to avoid the aforementioned confusion. (See the statement of Abu Ishaq al-Shatibi coming in paragraph 1/19 that it is permissible in language to attribute to the plural absolutely. (Ref: Hashiyat al-Sabban on al-Ashmuni in the discussion of the ya' of attribution. 29
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is the preface (khutbat al-kitab) from Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa's 'al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm'. The author opens by diagnosing a critical problem in legal education: students entering law school confront fiqh rulings as isolated branch issues (furu') without first understanding the underlying rules, causes, and principles, forcing them to memorize without grasping the theoretical connections. He argues that existing fiqh books and commentaries on the Majalla serve only as court references, not as pedagogical texts. He calls for new books written with an objective (mawdu'i) methodology: simplified, focused, and organized to meet the educational needs of universities as distinct from the practical needs of courts. He then recounts his personal mission: since being appointed to teach civil law based on the Majalla at the Syrian Law School in 1944, he resolved to adopt this necessary approach. The book he presents is a serial work on obligations and contracts in Islamic fiqh, covering the general civil rulings from the Majalla plus related important issues, with attention to later legal amendments. He explicitly adopts the Hanafi school as the basis because it is applied in the judiciary, while consulting other schools where needed. His ultimate aim is to reframe Islamic fiqh by constructing a general theory from its rules and principles, parallel to the general theory of obligations in modern Western legal systems, thereby revealing the precious essence of Islamic jurisprudence that had been obscured by the obsolete style. The footnote on 'furu'i' is a philological note justifying his use of the plural form in 'al-uslub al-furu'i' to avoid confusion with 'far'i' meaning secondary.

Key Terms
المنهج الموضوعي (al-manhaj al-mawḍū‘ī): The objective research method: presenting fiqh rulings and principles organized by subject matter rather than by enumerating branches, proceeding from simple to complex, and building a general theory.
الفروعي (al-furū‘ī): An adjective derived from the plural 'furu'' meaning branches; used to describe the traditional method of teaching fiqh by listing subsidiary issues without building them on a general theory. The author justifies this plural attribution to avoid confusion with 'far'i' (subsidiary as opposed to original).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Zarqa, what is the primary reason existing fiqh books are unsuitable for university teaching?
A) They are written in classical Arabic that students cannot understand.
B) They present branch issues without first teaching the rules, causes, and principles on which those branches depend.
C) They rely on multiple madhhabs and confuse students.
D) They are too long and detailed for a one-semester course.

Key Takeaway
Al-Zarqa's objective method transforms fiqh pedagogy from branch-based memorization to principle-based understanding, revealing the theoretical essence of Islamic law.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Pedagogical Failure of the Traditional Furu'i Method
Author explains the pedagogical flaw of the furu'i method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the shortcomings of the traditional furu'i method as identified by Mustafa al-Zarqa and explain why it creates obstacles for university students.

Core Idea
The branch-based method hides the universal principles, making fiqh obscure for beginners.

In the preface of Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm, Mustafa al-Zarqa diagnoses a critical issue: the traditional way of teaching fiqh by enumerating branch rulings (furu') without linking them to overarching theories leaves students confused. He argues that this 'furu'i style' has become indigestible for modern learners. This lesson unpacks that diagnosis.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Traditional Furu'i Method
Identify the method described by al-Zarqa as 'uslub furu'i' — listing individual rulings without a unifying framework.
He contrasts it with a theoretical approach (nazariyya 'amma).
2
Identify the Core Problem
Al-Zarqa states that furu'i issues are connected to universal principles (usul kulliyya) and general theories, but these are scattered across fiqh chapters.
Example: theory of ownership appears in multiple chapters.
3
Understand the Student's Struggle
A beginner does not have an overview of these principles, so each new ruling seems isolated and hard to grasp.
He compares it to needing a long journey through all chapters to gain understanding.
4
Recognize the Call for Reform
Al-Zarqa proposes building from rules and principles to create general theories, making fiqh accessible.
This sets the stage for his Madkhal.

Source Text

خطبة الكتاب
المهمة، مع الإشارة إلى التعديلات القانونية الطارئة على الأحكام الفقهية الأصلية منذ العهد العثماني في هذه البلاد السورية إلى اليوم.
وقد اتخذت فيه المذهب الحنفي في الفقه الإسلامي أساساً للبحث لأنه المعمول به في القضاء، مع الإلمام بالمذاهب الأخرى في بعض
المواطن بحسب حاجة البحث .
وهدفي فيه أن أقلب صياغة الفقه الإسلامي، فأبني من قواعده ومبادئه
نظرية عامة على غرار نظرية الإلتزام العامة في الفقه القانوني الأجنبي الحديث (۱) خدمة لفقهنا الإسلامي الجليل كي يتجلى ما فيه من جوهر نفيس كان محجوباً بالأسلوب القديم الذي أصبح عسير الهضم على رجال العصر ؛ ووفاء للحاجة إلى الطريقة التعليمية الحكيمة في الدراسة الجامعية لهذا العلم الدقيق المسائل المتشعب المباحث الواسع الآفاق، العظيم الشأن والموقع ذلك لأن الحقوق المدنية التي يطلق عليها اسم «القانون المدني» هي أس الدراسات والمدارك الحقوقية جميعاً، وأن الحاجة التعليمية فيها توجب طريقة موضوعية تسير من البسيط إلى المركب، ولم يعد يهضم فيها الأسلوب الفروعي (۲) القديم الذي لا تُقام فيه الفروع على أصولها في ·
نظرية كلية جامعة .
(1) ينظر التعريف بنظرية الإلتزام العامة الأجنبية في الجزء الثالث من هذه السلسلة. (۲) تسوغ النسبة إلى لفظ الجمع إذا صارت صيغته في الاستعمال كاسم العلم مثل (أنصاري) في النسبة إلى (الأنصار)، وكذا إذا كانت النسبة إلى المفرد تلبس المعنى المراد بغيره كما هنا، إذ لو قيل (فرعي) لما فهم منه معنى طريقة سرد الفروع، بل يفهم منه ما يقابل معنى (أصلي). ومثل ذلك في العرف القانوني اليوم كلمة (حقوقي) نسبة إلى الحقوق بمعنى العلم، فلو نسب إلى المفرد فقيل : (حقي) لالتبس المعنى المراد بغيره. وقد استعمل قدماء الفقهاء والأصوليين النسبة إلى (الفروع) بصيغة الجمع، فقالوا : فروعي إما باعتبار أن لفظ «الفرع صار كاسم علم المسائل الفقه، وإما لدفع الالتباس المذكور (انظر عبارة أبي إسحاق الشاطبي الآتية في الفقرة (۱/۱۹ ) على أنه يجوز في لغة أن ينسب إلى الجمع مطلقاً. (ر: حاشية الصبان على الأشموني في بحث ياء النسب).
۲۹
وقد كان من أعظم الأسباب في استغلاق الفقه على الطلاب خلال دراستهم الجامعية أن مسائله الفرعية تتصل بأصول كلية ونظريات عامة أساسية، يشترك في العلاقة بكل منها كثير من أبواب الفقه، ويتوقف على الإحاطة بها فهم مسائله وأحكامه، والطالب في بَدء دراسته يجهلها جميعاً. وذلك كنظرية الملكية وأنواعها وأسبابها ونظرية الارتباط التعاقدي، أي العقود، وما ترتكز عليه من أسس عامة ؛ ونظرية الشروط العقدية من تعليق وتقييد وإضافة ؛ ونظرية المؤيدات التشريعية وما يتفرع عنها في الحقل المدني من قضية البطلان والفساد والتوقف ؛ ونظرية الأهلية ؛ ونظرية الضمان ؛ ونظرية العزف وسلطانه، ونحو ذلك من المبادىء الأساسية والنظريات الموضوعية الكبرى التي هي من أركان الفقه ودعائم أحكامه، وهي منثورة الأجزاء في غضون الأبواب الفقهية يذكر منها في كل باب ما يتعلق به، ولكنها يمكن أن تقتطف أجزاؤها وتجمع من أماكنها وتصاغ منها سلسلة نظريات يصدر بها علم الفقه فتكون مفاتيح لأغلاق مسائله وتزود الطالب فيه بملكة في الفهم عاجلة كان يحتاج في اكتسابها إلى سير طويل في جميع فصول الفقه لذلك رأيت من الضروري أن أقدم بين يدي هذه السلسلة الفقهية
مدخلاً فقهياً عاماً يشتمل على ثلاثة أقسام :
١ - مقدمة تعريفية وتاريخية عن الفقه الإسلامي، ومصادره، ونشأة المذاهب الاجتهادية فيه وأسباب اختلافاتها وقيمة تلك الاختلافات في الثروة التشريعية وحركة التدوين فيه وطبقات مؤلفاته إلى بروز المجلة وعن سَعَة هذا الفقه الإسلامي بمجموع اجتهاداته وعن تطوره وصلوحه لوفاء حاجات العصور إذا أريدت الاستفادة منه، وجاد عليه الباحثون المعنيون بخدمة جديدة وحراثة حديثة يجود على أثرها بما في مناجمه من ثروة دفينة، ومعادن ثمينة.
۲ - النظريات الأساسية في مباني الأحكام الفقهية.
وهي النظم والركائز التأسيسية الكبرى التي تعتبر دعائم الفقه وأركانه وأشرنا آنفاً إلى ضرورة جمعها وتصدير الفقه بها.
۳۰
Preface of the Book: important, with reference to the legal amendments that affected original fiqh rulings since the Ottoman era in these Syrian lands up to today. I have taken the Hanafi madhhab in Islamic fiqh as the basis for research because it is the one followed in the judiciary, while also being acquainted with other madhhabs in some places according to the need of the research. My aim in it is to revamp the formulation of Islamic fiqh, so that I build from its rules and principles a general theory similar to the general theory of obligations in modern foreign legal jurisprudence (1) in service of our noble Islamic fiqh, so that its precious essence that was hidden by the old style, which has become difficult for contemporary people to digest, may become manifest; and in fulfillment of the need for a wise educational method in university study of this science of precise issues, diverse topics, wide horizons, great importance and position. That is because civil rights, which are called 'civil law,' are the foundation of all legal studies and understandings, and the educational need therein necessitates an objective method that proceeds from simple to complex, and the old branch-based style (2) in which branches are not built upon their principles within a comprehensive general theory is no longer digestible. (1) See the definition of the foreign general theory of obligations in the third part of this series. (2) It is permissible to attribute to the plural form when its usage becomes like a proper noun, such as 'Ansari' in attribution to 'Ansar'; likewise when attributing to the singular would confuse the intended meaning with something else, as here, for if one said 'far'i', the meaning of the method of enumerating branches would not be understood, but rather understood as contrasting with 'asli'. Similar in today's legal custom is the word 'huquqi' as an attribution to 'huquq' meaning science; if one attributed to the singular and said 'haqqi', the intended meaning would be confused. The early jurists and usulis used attribution to 'furu' in the plural form; they said 'furu'i', either because the word 'far'' became like a proper noun for the issues of fiqh, or to avoid the aforementioned confusion (see the statement of Abu Ishaq al-Shatibi later in paragraph 1/19) and it is permissible in the language to attribute to the plural absolutely (see: Hashiyat al-Saban 'ala al-Ashmuni in the section on ya' al-nisba). One of the greatest reasons for the obscurity of fiqh to students during their university studies is that its branch issues are connected to universal principles and basic general theories, many chapters of fiqh share in the relationship with each of them, and understanding its issues and rulings depends on encompassing them, while the student at the beginning of his study is ignorant of all of them. Such as the theory of ownership and its types and causes, the theory of contractual connection (i.e. contracts) and the general foundations upon which they are based; the theory of contractual conditions of suspension, restriction, and addition; the theory of legal supports and what branches from them in the civil field of invalidity, corruption, and suspension; the theory of legal capacity; the theory of guarantee; the theory of disposal and its authority; and similar fundamental principles and major objective theories that are pillars of fiqh and supports of its rulings. Their parts are scattered throughout the chapters of fiqh; in each chapter what pertains to it is mentioned, but their parts can be plucked and gathered from their places and a series of theories can be formulated that preface the science of fiqh, thus being keys to the locks of its issues and providing the student with a quick ability in understanding that he used to need a long journey through all the chapters of fiqh to acquire. Therefore I saw it necessary to present before this fiqh series a general fiqh introduction (Madkhal Fiqhi 'Amm) comprising three sections: 1 - An introductory and historical overview of Islamic fiqh, its sources, the emergence of ijtihad schools within it, the reasons for their differences, the value of those differences in legislative wealth, the movement of codification in it, the strata of its authors up to the emergence of the Majalla, and about the breadth of this Islamic fiqh with all its ijtihadat, its development and its suitability to meet the needs of the times if one wishes to benefit from it, and if concerned researchers bestow upon it new service and modern cultivation that yields the hidden wealth in its mines and precious minerals. 2 - The basic theories in the foundations of fiqh rulings. They are the great foundational systems and pillars that are considered the supports and pillars of fiqh, and we have already pointed out the necessity of gathering them and prefacing fiqh with them.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface (خطبة الكتاب) to al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The author opens by stating that his work takes the Hanafi madhhab as the primary basis because it is the official school applied in the judiciary, though he also references other madhhabs where needed. His main objective is to re-formulate Islamic fiqh by constructing general theories from its rules and principles, analogous to the general theory of obligations in modern Western legal systems. He argues that the traditional branch-based (فروعي) style of fiqh, which lists individual rulings without linking them to overarching principles, has become indigestible for contemporary students. The author identifies the root cause of students' difficulty: fiqh's branch issues are connected to universal principles (أصول كلية) and general theories, but these are dispersed across various chapters, so a beginner cannot see the big picture. He lists examples of such theories: ownership, contracts, contractual conditions (suspension, restriction, addition), legal validity/invalidity, legal capacity, guarantee, and the authority of disposal. These are the pillars of fiqh. By gathering them into a coherent series, he aims to provide a key to understanding fiqh and accelerate the student's grasp. Therefore, he introduces his 'General Fiqh Introduction' (مدخل فقهي عام) divided into three sections, though only two are fully listed here: (1) an introductory and historical overview covering sources, madhhabs, codification, and the Majalla; (2) the basic theories underlying fiqh rulings. The third section presumably follows on the next page. This preface sets the stage for a modern, systematic, and pedagogical presentation of Hanafi fiqh, focusing on general theories rather than isolated cases.

Key Terms
نظرية عامة (nazariyya 'amma): A comprehensive theoretical framework built from fiqh rules and principles, analogous to a 'general theory' in modern legal systems (e.g., the general theory of obligations).
أسلوب فروعي (uslub furu'i): The traditional method of presenting fiqh by enumerating individual branch rulings (furu') without explicitly linking them to overarching principles or theories.
مدخل فقهي عام (madkhal fiqhi 'amm): A general introduction to fiqh that presents the foundational theories and principles before delving into specific chapters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Mustafa al-Zarqa, what is one of the greatest reasons for the obscurity of fiqh to university students?
A) The lack of qualified teachers
B) The branch issues are connected to universal principles that are scattered and not presented first
C) The rulings are too numerous to memorize
D) The Hanafi madhhab is too difficult

Key Takeaway
The traditional furu'i method obscures the universal principles of fiqh; presenting general theories first is essential for effective learning.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Al-Zarqa's Solution: General Theories and the Madkhal Structure
Author outlines his proposed work: a general fiqh introduction with three sections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the three components of al-Zarqa's 'General Fiqh Introduction' and explain how each addresses the pedagogical problems of the furu'i method.

Core Idea
Al-Zarqa proposes reconstructing fiqh around central theories, making it accessible and systematic.

After diagnosing the problems of the furu'i method, Mustafa al-Zarqa presents his solution: a general fiqh introduction (Madkhal Fiqhi 'Amm) that gathers the scattered theories and presents them upfront. This lesson examines the structure he proposes and its educational rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Sections of the Madkhal
Al-Zarqa outlines three sections: (1) historical/introductory overview, (2) basic theories of fiqh rulings, (3) [implied: application or further theories]. Note the first two are detailed.
The third section is mentioned but not described in this excerpt.
2
Understand the Purpose of Section 1
Section 1 covers history, sources, madhhabs, codification up to the Majalla, and the breadth of fiqh. It provides context and a big picture.
This addresses the student's need for orientation.
3
Understand the Purpose of Section 2
Section 2 presents the basic theories (nazariyyaat) that underlie all fiqh rulings, such as ownership, contracts, conditions, etc.
These are the 'keys to the locks' of issues.
4
Connect Each Section to the Problem
The furu'i method scattered theories; section 2 gathers them. The furu'i method lacked context; section 1 provides history. The result is a structured, top-down presentation.
Al-Zarqa aims to give students a 'quick ability in understanding'.
